Emmanuel Gnabeyeu111Laboratoire de Probabilit√©s, Statistique et Mod√©lisation, UMR 8001, Sorbonne Universit√© and Universit√© Paris Cit√©, 4 pl. Jussieu, F-75252 Paris Cedex 5, France. E-mail: emmanuel.gnabeyeu\_mbiada@sorbonne-universite.fr222This research benefited from the support of ‚ÄĚEcole Doctorale Sciences Mathematiques de Paris Centre‚ÄĚ.

###### Abstract

This paper is concerned with Merton‚Äôs portfolio optimization problem in a Volterra stochastic environment described by a multivariate fake stationary Volterra‚ÄďHeston model.
Due to the non-Markovianity and non-semimartingality of the underlying processes, the classical stochastic control
approach cannot be directly applied in this setting. Instead, the problem is tackled using a stochastic factor solution to a Riccati backward stochastic differential equation (BSDE).
Our approach is inspired by the martingale optimality principle combined with a suitable verification argument. The resulting optimal strategies for Merton‚Äôs problems are derived in semi-closed form depending on the solutions to time-dependent multivariate Riccati-Volterra equations.
Numerical results on a two dimensional fake stationary rough Heston model illustrate the impact
of stationary rough volatilities on the optimal Merton strategies.

Keywords: Affine Volterra Processes, Stochastic Control, Martingale Optimality Principle, Backward Stochastic Differential Equations (BSDE), Fractional Differential Equations, Riccati Equations, Functional Integral Equation.

Mathematics Subject Classification (2020):  34A08, 34A34, 45D05, 60G10, 60G22, 60H10, 91B70, 91G80,93E20

## 1 Introduction

The modeling of asset price dynamics has undergone a paradigm shift with the empirical observation that both implied and realized volatilities of major financial indices exhibit significantly rougher sample paths (Gatheral et al., [2018](#bib.bib13)) than those generated by classical Brownian-motion-based models. This observation has sparked a rapidly expanding body of research on rough volatility models. Motivated by the widespread practical success of the celebrated Heston ([1993](#bib.bib20)) stochastic volatility framework, several rough extensions have been proposed, most notably the rough Heston model (El Euch and Rosenbaum, [2019](#bib.bib11)) builds on market microstructure and its generalisation, the Volterra Heston model in Abi Jaber et al. ([2019](#bib.bib1)). Recent remarkable advances include the introduction of the so-called fake stationary Volterra Heston models in Gnabeyeu et al. ([a](#bib.bib16), [b](#bib.bib17)) with the aim of providing a unified and consistent framework that captures both short- and long-maturity behaviors and enables robust fitting across the entire term structure. This broader class of volatility models, encompassing the aforementioned specifications, is obtained by modeling the volatility process as a stochastic Volterra equation of convolution type with a time-dependent diffusion coefficient. Therefore, this paper focuses on the financial market within the fake stationary affine Volterra model.

Substantial progress has recently been achieved in the study of option pricing problems and asymptotic analysis under rough volatility dynamics. By contrast, portfolio optimization in such models remains comparatively underexplored, although it has attracted growing interest in recent years.
Notable contributions include Fouque and Hu ([2019](#bib.bib12)); B√§uerle and Desmettre ([2020](#bib.bib5)); Han and Wong ([2020](#bib.bib19)), which investigate optimal investment problems with power utility in fractional Heston-type models. Despite these advances, the overwhelming majority of developments in rough volatility, whether for asset modeling, derivative pricing, or portfolio selection, have been confined to the mono-asset case. From a practical standpoint, however, multi-asset allocation with correlated sources of risk constitutes a fundamental dimension of portfolio management; see, for instance, Buraschi et al. ([2010](#bib.bib7)).

Merton‚Äôs portfolio optimization problem which consists in maximizing an investor‚Äôs expected utility from terminal wealth with respect to a given utility function has served as a cornerstone in mathematical finance. It is the most classic financial economic approach to understand how the market volatility affect investment demands.
In the classical Heston ([1993](#bib.bib20)) stochastic volatility framework, this problem was solved explicitly in Kraft ([2005](#bib.bib25)), building on the representation results of Zariphopoulou ([2001](#bib.bib34)), and extensions to general affine stochastic volatility models were obtained in Kallsen and Muhle-Karbe ([2010](#bib.bib24)) using stochastic control theory.
In the Volterra framework, however, the volatility process is non-Markovian, which prevents the direct application of the classical stochastic control methods based on the Hamilton‚ÄďJacobi‚ÄďBellman (HJB) partial differential equation.
In order to circumvent this difficulty, Han and Wong ([2020](#bib.bib19)), inspired by Fouque and Hu ([2019](#bib.bib12)), adopt a martingale distortion ansatz and apply the martingale optimality principle to derive explicit optimal investment strategies in a single-asset or mono-asset Volterra‚ÄďHeston model.

Motivated by several important empirical stylized facts about real financial markets such as choice among multiple assets, rough volatility behavior, correlations across stocks or assets and leverage effects (i.e., correlation between
a stock and its volatility), multivariate rough volatility models have recently been developed ; see, e.g., Abi Jaber et al. ([2019](#bib.bib1)); Tomas and Rosenbaum ([2021](#bib.bib31)).
In Aichinger and Desmettre ([2021](#bib.bib3)), the authors analyze the Merton portfolio problems with power utility for a class of multivariate Volterra Heston models that features both inter-asset correlations and correlation between a
stock and its volatility.
In the present paper, we solve the Merton portfolio problem for investors with power and exponential utility functions, within the class of the so-called fake stationary multivariate affine Volterra models.

Main contributions.
Building upon recent developments in volatility and Volterra models (Gnabeyeu et al., [2024](#bib.bib18), [a](#bib.bib16), [b](#bib.bib17)) and motivated by recent works and advances on multivariate Volterra volatility modeling Abi Jaber et al. ([2019](#bib.bib1)); Tomas and Rosenbaum ([2021](#bib.bib31)); Aichinger and Desmettre ([2021](#bib.bib3)), the primary objective of this paper is to advance the literature on utility maximization along two main directions:

* (i)

  We introduce a class of  multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra stochastic volatility models that capture key stylized features of financial markets, including heterogeneous roughness across assets, possibly stochastic inter-asset correlations, and leverage effects namely, dependence between asset returns and their respective volatilities while maintaining a consistent modeling framework across time scales, from short to long maturities.
* (ii)

  This model preserve analytical tractability, thereby enabling explicit characterization of the optimal investment strategy for the Merton‚Äôs problem, despite the intrinsic challenges posed by multivariate non-Markovian dynamics.

Organization of the Work.
The outline of the paper is as follows: Section [2](#S2 "2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models") gives an overview of the model which is needed throughout the paper: We introduce the multi asset financial
market, where volatility is modeled by a multivariate class of fake stationary Volterra square root process, and we state the optimization problem. For such a market model we consider in section [3](#S3 "3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")
two different approaches to solve the Merton portfolio problem. More precisely, in section [3](#S3 "3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models") we investigate the classical problem of maximizing the expected utility of terminal wealth in a multi-asset fake stationary Volterra‚ÄďHeston volatility market, for both power and exponential utility preferences.
We first adapt the martingale distortion transformation used in Fouque and Hu ([2019](#bib.bib12)); Han and Wong ([2020](#bib.bib19)) to the (degenerate) multivariate case. However, as it is pointed out in Abi Jaber et al. ([2021](#bib.bib2)); Aichinger and Desmettre ([2021](#bib.bib3)), this only works if the correlation structure is highly degenerate.
Inspired by the techniques
used in B√§uerle and Li ([2013](#bib.bib6)); Aichinger and Desmettre ([2021](#bib.bib3)), we then provide a solution for the Merton portfolio optimization problem for a more general correlation structure using a verification argument. In Section [4](#S4 "4 Numerical experiments: The particular case of the fake stationary rough Heston volatility ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models"), we demonstrate the practical implications of our findings through numerical experiments based on a two-dimensional fake stationary rough Heston model. Finally, Section [5](#S5 "5 Proofs of the main results ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models") is devoted to the proofs of the main results.

thus, it can be a strictly larger filtration. Here ‚Ąô\mathbb{P} is a real-world probability measure from which a family of equivalent probability measures can be generated.

## 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models

Fix T>0T>0, d‚ąą‚Ąēd\in\mathbb{N}.
We let K=diag‚Ā°(K1,‚Ä¶,Kd)K=\operatorname{diag}(K\_{1},\ldots,K\_{d}) be diagonal with scalar kernels Ki‚ąąL2‚Äč([0,T],‚ĄĚ)K\_{i}\in L^{2}([0,T],\mathbb{R}) on the diagonal, ŌÜ=diag‚Ā°(ŌÜ1,‚Ä¶,ŌÜd)\varphi=\operatorname{diag}(\varphi^{1},\ldots,\varphi^{d}), őĹ=diag‚Ā°(őĹ1,‚Ä¶,őĹd)\nu=\operatorname{diag}(\nu\_{1},\ldots,\nu\_{d}), Ōā=diag‚Ā°(Ōā1,‚Ä¶,Ōād)\varsigma=\operatorname{diag}(\varsigma^{1},\ldots,\varsigma^{d}) with Ōāi\varsigma^{i} a (locally) bounded Borel function and D:=‚ąídiag‚Ā°(őĽ1,‚Ä¶,őĽd)‚ąą‚ĄĚd√ódD:=-\operatorname{diag}(\lambda\_{1},\ldots,\lambda\_{d})\in\mathbb{R}^{d\times d}.
Let V=(V1,‚Ä¶,Vd)‚ä§V=(V^{1},\ldots,V^{d})^{\top} be the following ‚ĄĚ+d\mathbb{R}^{d}\_{+}‚Äďvalued scaled Volterra square‚Äďroot process driven by an dd-dimensional process W=(W1,‚Ä¶,Wd)‚ä§W=(W^{1},\ldots,W^{d})^{\top}:

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | Vt=ŌÜ(t)V0+‚ąę0tK(t‚ąís)(őľ(s)+DVs)ds+‚ąę0tK(t‚ąís)őĹŌā(s)diag‚Ā°(Vs)dWs,V0‚üā‚üāW.\displaystyle V\_{t}=\varphi(t)V\_{0}+\int\_{0}^{t}K(t-s)\big(\mu(s)+DV\_{s}\big)ds+\int\_{0}^{t}K(t-s)\nu\varsigma(s)\sqrt{\operatorname{diag}(V\_{s})}dW\_{s},\quad V\_{0}\perp\!\!\!\perp W. |  | (2.2) |

Here őľ:‚ĄĚ+‚Üí‚ĄĚd\mu:\mathbb{R}\_{+}\to\mathbb{R}^{d}, WW is a dd-dimensional Wiener process.
Note that the drift b‚Äč(t,x)=őľ‚Äč(t)+D‚Äčxb(t,x)=\mu(t)+Dx is clearly Lipschitz continuous in x‚ąą‚ĄĚdx\in\mathbb{R}^{d}, uniformly in t‚ąąūĚēč+t\!\in\mathbb{T}\_{+} and both the drift term bb and the diffusion coefficient ŌÉ‚Äč(t,x)=őĹ‚ÄčŌā‚Äč(t)‚Äčdiag‚Ā°(x)\sigma(t,x)=\nu\varsigma(t)\sqrt{\operatorname{diag}(x)} are of linear growth, i.e. there is a constant Cb,ŌÉ>0C\_{b,\sigma}>0 such that

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | ‚ÄĖb‚Äč(t,x)‚ÄĖ+‚ÄĖ|ŌÉ‚Äč(t,x)|‚ÄĖ‚Č§Cb,ŌÉ‚Äč(1+‚ÄĖx‚ÄĖ),for all¬†‚Äčt‚ąą[0,T]‚Äč¬†and¬†‚Äčx‚ąą‚ĄĚ.\|b(t,x)\|+\||\sigma(t,x)|\|\leq C\_{b,\sigma}(1+\|x\|),\quad\text{for all }t\in[0,T]\text{ and }x\in\mathbb{R}. |  |

We always work under the assumption below, which applies to the inhomogeneous Volterra equation ([2.2](#S2.E2 "In 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")).

###### Assumption 2.1 (On Volterra Equations with convolutive kernels).

Assume that KK is diagonal with scalar kernels KiK\_{i} on the diagonal for i=1,‚Ä¶,di=1,\ldots,d that is completely monotone on (0,‚ąě)(0,\infty) and satisfy for any T>0T>0,

1. (i)

   Assume that the kernel KiK\_{i} is strictly positive and satisfy:

   * ‚ÄĒ

     The integrability assumption: The following is satisfied for some őł^i‚ąą(0,1]\widehat{\theta}\_{i}\in(0,1].

     |  |  |  |  |
     | --- | --- | --- | --- |
     |  | (ūĚí¶^őł^c‚Äčo‚Äčn‚Äčt)‚Äč‚ąÉőļi^<+‚ąě,‚ąÄőī¬Į‚ąą(0,T],ő∑^‚Äč(őī):=supt‚ąą[0,T][‚ąę(t‚ąíőī¬Į)+tKi‚Äč(t‚ąíu)2‚ÄčūĚĎĎu]12‚Č§őļ^i‚Äčőī¬Įőł^i.(\widehat{\cal K}^{cont}\_{\widehat{\theta}})\;\;\exists\,\widehat{\kappa\_{i}}<+\infty,\;\forall\bar{\delta}\!\in(0,T],\;\widehat{\eta}(\delta):=\sup\_{t\in[0,T]}\left[\int\_{(t-\bar{\delta})^{+}}^{t}\thinspace K\_{i}\big(t-u\big)^{2}du\right]^{\frac{1}{2}}\leq\widehat{\kappa}\_{i}\,\bar{\delta}^{\,\widehat{\theta}\_{i}}. |  | (2.3) |
   * ‚ÄĒ

     The continuity assumption: (ūĚí¶őłc‚Äčo‚Äčn‚Äčt)‚Äč‚ąÉőļi<+‚ąě,‚ąÉőłi‚ąą(0,1]‚Äčsuch that‚Äč‚ąÄőī¬Į‚ąą(0,T)({\cal K}^{cont}\_{\theta})\;\;\exists\,\kappa\_{i}<+\infty,\;\exists\;\theta\_{i}\in(0,1]\;\text{such that}\;\forall\,\bar{\delta}{\in(0,T)}

     |  |  |  |  |
     | --- | --- | --- | --- |
     |  | (ūĚí¶őłc‚Äčo‚Äčn‚Äčt)‚Äč‚ąÄőī¬Į‚ąą(0,T),ő∑‚Äč(őī¬Į):=supt‚ąą[0,T][‚ąę0t|Ki‚Äč((s+őī)‚ąßT)‚ąíKi‚Äč(s)|2‚ÄčūĚĎĎs]12‚Č§őļi‚Äčőī¬Įőłi.({\cal K}^{cont}\_{\theta})\;\forall\,\bar{\delta}{\,\in(0,T)},\;\eta(\bar{\delta}):=\sup\_{t\in[0,T]}\left[\int\_{0}^{t}|K\_{i}(\big(s+\delta)\wedge T\big)-K\_{i}(s)|^{2}ds\right]^{\frac{1}{2}}\leq\kappa\_{i}\,\bar{\delta}^{\theta\_{i}}. |  | (2.4) |
2. (ii)

   Finally, assume that V0i‚ąąLp‚Äč(‚Ąô)V\_{0}^{i}\in L^{p}(\mathbb{P}) for some suitable p‚ąą(0,+‚ąě)p\in(0,+\infty), such that
   the process t‚Üív0i‚Äč(t)=V0‚ÄčŌÜi‚Äč(t)t\to v\_{0}^{i}(t)=V\_{0}\varphi^{i}(t) is absolutely continuous and (‚ĄĪt)(\mathcal{F}\_{t})-adapted.
   Moreover, for some őīi>0\delta\_{i}>0, for any p>0p>0,

   |  |  |  |
   | --- | --- | --- |
   |  | ūĚĒľ‚Äč(supt‚ąą[0,T]|v0i‚Äč(t)|p)<+‚ąě,ūĚĒľ‚Äč[|v0i‚Äč(t‚Ä≤)‚ąív0i‚Äč(t)|p]‚Č§CT,p‚Äč(1+ūĚĒľ‚Äč[supt‚ąą[0,T]|v0i‚Äč(t)|p])‚Äč|t‚Ä≤‚ąít|őīi‚Äčp.\mathbb{E}\,\!\Big(\sup\_{t\in[0,T]}|v\_{0}^{i}(t)|^{p}\Big)<+\infty,\quad\mathbb{E}\!\big[\,|v\_{0}^{i}(t^{\prime})-v\_{0}^{i}(t)|^{p}\,\big]\leq C\_{T,p}\Big(1+\mathbb{E}\,\big[\sup\_{t\in[0,T]}|v\_{0}^{i}(t)|^{p}\big]\Big)|t^{\prime}-t|^{\delta\_{i}p}. |  |

Remark: For i=1,‚Ä¶,di=1,\ldots,d , as KiK\_{i} is completely monotone on (0,‚ąě)(0,\infty) and not identically zero, we have that
KiK\_{i} is nonnegative, not identically zero, non-increasing and continuous on (0,‚ąě)(0,\infty), and it follows from (B. Gripenberg and Saavalainen, [1990](#bib.bib4), Theorem 5.5.4) that KiK\_{i} has a resolvent of the first kind rir\_{i} which is nonnegative and non-increasing in the sense that s‚Ü¶ri‚Äč([s,s+t])s\mapsto r\_{i}([s,s+t])
is non-increasing for all t‚Č•0t\geq 0.

In the case of őĪ‚ąí\alpha- fractional kernel (corresponding to Ki=KőĪiK\_{i}=K\_{\alpha\_{i}} with őĪi‚ąą[12,1)\alpha\_{i}\in[\frac{1}{2},1)), by Gnabeyeu et al. ([b](#bib.bib17)) Equation ([2.2](#S2.E2 "In 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) admits at least a unique-in-law positive weak solution as a scaling limit of a sequence of
time-modulated Hawkes processes with heavy-tailed kernels in a nearly unstable regime.
Moreover, under assumption [2.1](#S2.Thmassumption1 "Assumption 2.1 (On Volterra Equations with convolutive kernels). ‚Ä£ 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models") for some p>0p>0, a solution t‚Ü¶Vtt\mapsto V\_{t} to Equation ([2.2](#S2.E2 "In 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) starting from V0V\_{0}
has a (őī‚ąßŌĎ‚ąßő≤‚ąí12‚Äčő≤‚ąíő∑)\big(\delta\wedge\vartheta\wedge\frac{\beta-1}{2\beta}-\eta\big)-H√∂lder pathwise continuous modification on ‚ĄĚ+d\mathbb{R}\_{+}^{d} for sufficiently small ő∑>0\eta>0 and satisfying (among other properties),

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | ‚ąÄT>0,‚ąÉCT,p>0,‚ÄĖsupt‚ąą[0,T]‚ÄĖVt‚ÄĖ‚ÄĖp‚Č§CT,p‚Äč(1+‚ÄĖsupt‚ąą[0,T]‚ÄĖŌÜ‚Äč(t)‚ÄčV0‚ÄĖ‚ÄĖp).\forall\,T>0,\;\exists\,C\_{{}\_{T,p}}>0,\quad\big\|\sup\_{t\in[0,T]}\|V\_{t}\|\big\|\_{p}\leq C\_{{}\_{T,p}}\left(1+\big\|\sup\_{t\in[0,T]}\|\varphi(t)V\_{0}\|\big\|\_{p}\right). |  | (2.5) |

Note that under our assumptions, if p>0p>0 and ūĚĒľ‚Äč[‚ÄĖŌÜ‚Äč(t)‚ÄčV0‚ÄĖp]<+‚ąě\mathbb{E}[\|\varphi(t)V\_{0}\|^{p}]<+\infty for every t‚Č•0t\geq 0, then by ([2.5](#S2.E5 "In 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")), ūĚĒľ‚Äč[supt‚ąą[0,T]‚ÄĖVt‚ÄĖp]<CT‚Äč(1+ūĚĒľ‚Äč[supt‚ąą[0,T]‚ÄĖŌÜ‚Äč(t)‚ÄčV0‚ÄĖp])<+‚ąě\mathbb{E}[\sup\_{t\in[0,T]}\|V\_{t}\|^{p}]<C\_{T}(1+\mathbb{E}[\sup\_{t\in[0,T]}\|\varphi(t)V\_{0}\|^{p}])<+\infty for every T>0T>0. Combined with the linear growth in Assumption [2.1](#S2.Thmassumption1 "Assumption 2.1 (On Volterra Equations with convolutive kernels). ‚Ä£ 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")(ii) ‚ÄĖ|ŌÉ‚Äč(t,x)|‚ÄĖ‚Č§CT‚Ä≤‚Äč(1+‚ÄĖx‚ÄĖ)\||\sigma(t,x)|\|\leq C^{\prime}\_{T}(1+\|x\|) for t‚ąą[0,T]t\in[0,T], this implies ūĚĒľ‚Äč[supt‚ąą[0,T]‚ÄĖ|ŌÉ‚Äč(t,Xt)|‚ÄĖp]<CT‚Ä≤‚Äč(1+ūĚĒľ‚Äč[supt‚ąą[0,T]‚ÄĖŌÜ‚Äč(t)‚ÄčV0‚ÄĖp])<+‚ąě\mathbb{E}[\sup\_{t\in[0,T]}\||\sigma(t,X\_{t})|\|^{p}]<C^{\prime}\_{T}(1+\mathbb{E}[\sup\_{t\in[0,T]}\|\varphi(t)V\_{0}\|^{p}])<+\infty for every T>0T>0, enabling the unrestricted use of both regular and stochastic Fubini‚Äôs theorems.
Sufficient conditions for interchanging the order of ordinary integration (with respect to a finite measure) and stochastic integration (with respect to a square integrable martingale) are provided in (Kailath et al., [1978](#bib.bib23), Thm.1), and further details can be found in (Protter, [2005](#bib.bib29), Thm. IV.65), (Walsh, [1986](#bib.bib33), Theorem 2.6), (Veraar, [2012](#bib.bib32), Theorem 2.6).

###### Remark 2.1.

This covers, for instance, constant non-negative kernels, fractional kernels of the form tőĪ‚ąí1őď‚Äč(őĪ)‚ÄčūĚüŹ‚ĄĚ+\frac{t^{\alpha-1}}{\Gamma(\alpha)}\mathbf{1}\_{\mathbb{R}\_{+}} with őĪ‚ąą(12,1]\alpha\in(\frac{1}{2},1], exponentially decaying kernels e‚ąíő≤‚Äčt{\rm e}^{-\beta t} with ő≤>0\beta>0 and more generally the gamma kernel K‚Äč(t)=tőĪ‚ąí1őď‚Äč(őĪ)‚Äče‚ąíő≤‚Äčt‚ÄčūĚüŹ‚ĄĚ+K(t)=\frac{t^{\alpha-1}}{\Gamma(\alpha)}e^{-\beta t}\mathbf{1}\_{\mathbb{R}\_{+}} with őĪ‚ąą(12,1]\alpha\in\left(\tfrac{1}{2},1\right] and ő≤‚Č•0\beta\geq 0 ( see e.g. (Gnabeyeu and Pag√®s, [2025](#bib.bib15), Propositions 6.1 and 6.3)).

The roughness of the volatility paths is determined by the parameter őĪ\alpha linked to the Hurst parameter HH via the relation őĪ=H+12\alpha=H+\frac{1}{2}.
For őĪ‚Üí1\alpha\rightarrow 1 we recover the classical markovian square root process.

### 2.1 Stabilizer and fake stationarity regimes.

###### Definition 2.2 (Fake Stationarity Regimes).

Let (Vt)t‚Č•0(V\_{t})\_{t\geq 0} be a solution to the scaled Volterra equation ([2.2](#S2.E2 "In 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) starting from any V0‚ąąL2‚Äč(‚Ąô)V\_{0}\in L^{2}(\mathbb{P}).
Then, the process (Vt)t‚Č•0(V\_{t})\_{t\geq 0} exhibit a fake stationary regime of type I in the sense of Pag√®s ([2024](#bib.bib27)); Gnabeyeu and Pag√®s ([2025](#bib.bib15)) if it has constant mean and variance over time i.e.:

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | ‚ąÄt‚Č•0,ūĚĒľ‚Äč[Vt]=cste‚Äčand‚ÄčVar‚Äč(Vt)=cste=v0‚ąą‚ĄĚ+d.\forall\,t\geq 0,\quad\mathbb{E}[V\_{t}]=\textit{c}^{\text{ste}}\quad\mbox{and}\quad\text{Var}(V\_{t})=\textit{c}^{\text{ste}}=v\_{0}\in\mathbb{R}\_{+}^{d}. |  | (2.6) |

For every őĽ‚ąą‚ĄĚ\lambda\!\in\mathbb{R}, the  resolvent or Solvent core RőĽR\_{\lambda} associated to a real-valued kernel KK, known as the  őĽ\lambda-resolvent of KK is defined as the unique solution ‚Äď if it exists ‚Äď to the deterministic Volterra equation

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | ‚ąÄt‚Č•0,RőĽ‚Äč(t)+őĽ‚Äč‚ąę0tK‚Äč(t‚ąís)‚ÄčRőĽ‚Äč(s)‚ÄčūĚĎĎs=1.\forall\,t\geq 0,\quad R\_{\lambda}(t)+\lambda\int\_{0}^{t}K(t-s)R\_{\lambda}(s)ds=1. |  | (2.7) |

or, equivalently, written in terms of convolution,
RőĽ+őĽ‚ÄčK‚ąóRőĽ=1R\_{\lambda}+\lambda K\*R\_{\lambda}=1 and admits the formal Neumann series expansion RőĽ=1‚ąó(‚ąĎk‚Č•0(‚ąí1)k‚ÄčőĽk‚ÄčKk‚Ā£‚ąó)R\_{\lambda}=\mbox{\bf 1}\*\big(\sum\_{k\geq 0}(-1)^{k}\lambda^{k}K^{k\*}\big)
where Kk‚Ā£‚ąóK^{k\*} denotes the kk-th convolution of KK with the convention, K0‚Ā£‚ąó=őī0K^{0\*}=\delta\_{0} (Dirac mass at 0).

Remark If KK is regular enough (say continuous) the resolvent RőĽR\_{\lambda} is differentiable and one checks that főĽ=‚ąíRőĽ‚Ä≤f\_{\lambda}=-R^{\prime}\_{\lambda} satisfies for every t>0t>0, ‚ąífőĽ‚Äč(t)+őĽ‚Äč(RőĽ‚Äč(0)‚ÄčK‚Äč(t)‚ąíK‚ąófőĽ‚Äč(t))=0-f\_{\lambda}(t)+\lambda\big(R\_{\lambda}(0)K(t)-K\*f\_{\lambda}(t)\big)=0
that is főĽf\_{\lambda} is solution to the equation

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | főĽ+őĽ‚ÄčK‚ąófőĽ=őĽ‚ÄčKand readsfőĽ=‚ąĎk‚Č•1(‚ąí1)k‚ÄčőĽk‚ÄčKk‚Ā£‚ąó,K0‚Ā£‚ąó=őī0.f\_{\lambda}+\lambda K\*f\_{\lambda}=\lambda K\quad\text{and reads}\quad f\_{\lambda}=\sum\_{k\geq 1}(-1)^{k}\lambda^{k}K^{k\*},\quad K^{0\*}=\delta\_{0}. |  | (2.8) |

###### Example 2.3.

Denote by EőĪE\_{\alpha} the standard Mittag-Leffler function. For the őĪ‚ąí\alpha-fractional kernels defined in Remark [2.1](#S2.ThmTheorem1 "Remark 2.1. ‚Ä£ 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models") the identity KőĪ‚ąóKőĪ‚Ä≤=KőĪ+őĪ‚Ä≤K\_{\alpha}\*K\_{\alpha^{\prime}}=K\_{\alpha+\alpha^{\prime}} holds for t‚Č•0t\geq 0 so that

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | RőĪ,őĽ‚Äč(t)=‚ąĎk‚Č•0(‚ąí1)k‚ÄčőĽk‚ÄčtőĪ‚Äčkőď‚Äč(őĪ‚Äčk+1)=EőĪ‚Äč(‚ąíőĽ‚ÄčtőĪ),and¬†‚ÄčfőĪ,őĽ‚Äč(t)=‚ąíRőĪ,őĽ‚Ä≤‚Äč(t)=őĽ‚ÄčtőĪ‚ąí1‚Äč‚ąĎk‚Č•0(‚ąí1)k‚ÄčőĽk‚ÄčtőĪ‚Äčkőď‚Äč(őĪ‚Äč(k+1)).R\_{\alpha,\lambda}(t)=\sum\_{k\geq 0}(-1)^{k}\frac{\lambda^{k}t^{\alpha k}}{\Gamma(\alpha k+1)}=E\_{\alpha}(-\lambda t^{\alpha}),\;\text{and }\;f\_{\alpha,\lambda}(t)=-R^{\prime}\_{\alpha,\lambda}(t)=\lambda t^{\alpha-1}\sum\_{k\geq 0}(-1)^{k}\lambda^{k}\frac{t^{\alpha k}}{\Gamma(\alpha(k+1))}. |  |

We will always work under the following assumption.

###### Assumption 2.2 (őĽ\lambda-resolvent RőĽR\_{\lambda} of the kernel).

For i=1,‚čĮ,di=1,\cdots,d, we assume that the őĽi\lambda\_{i}-resolvent RőĽiR\_{\lambda\_{i}} of the kernel KiK\_{i} satisfies the following for every őĽi>0\lambda\_{i}>0:

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | (ūĚí¶){(i)RőĽi(t)¬†is¬†differentiable on¬†‚ĄĚ+,RőĽi(0)=1¬†and¬†limt‚Üí+‚ąěRőĽi(t)=ai‚ąą[0,1[,(i‚Äči)főĽi‚ąą‚Ąíloc2(‚ĄĚ+,Leb1),¬†for¬†t>0,LfőĽi(t)‚Č†0dt‚ąía.e.,¬†where¬†főĽi:=‚ąíRőĽi‚Ä≤,(i‚Äči‚Äči)ŌÜi‚ąą‚Ąí‚ĄĚ+1‚Äč(Leb1),¬†is a continuous function satisfying‚Äčlimt‚Üí‚ąěŌÜi‚Äč(t)=ŌÜ‚ąěi,¬†with¬†‚Äčai‚ÄčŌÜ‚ąěi<1,(i‚Äčv)őľ‚Äč¬†is a¬†C1-function such that¬†‚Äč‚ÄĖőľ‚ÄĖsup<‚ąě‚Äč¬†and¬†‚Äčlimt‚Üí+‚ąěőľ‚Äč(t)=őľ‚ąě‚ąą‚ĄĚd.({\cal K})\quad\left\{\begin{array}[]{ll}(i)&R\_{\lambda\_{i}}(t)\text{ is }\text{differentiable on }\mathbb{R}^{+},\;R\_{\lambda\_{i}}(0)=1\text{ and }\lim\_{t\to+\infty}R\_{\lambda\_{i}}(t)=a\_{i}\in[0,1[,\\ (ii)&f\_{\lambda\_{i}}\in{\cal L}\_{\text{loc}}^{2}(\mathbb{R}\_{+},\text{Leb}\_{1}),\;\text{ for }\;t>0,\;L\_{f\_{\lambda\_{i}}}(t)\neq 0\;dt-a.e.,\text{ where }f\_{\lambda\_{i}}:=-R^{\prime}\_{\lambda\_{i}},\\ (iii)&\varphi^{i}\in{\cal L}^{1}\_{\mathbb{R}\_{+}}(\text{Leb}\_{1}),\text{ is a continuous function satisfying}\;\lim\_{t\to\infty}\varphi^{i}(t)=\varphi\_{\infty}^{i},\text{ with }a\_{i}\varphi\_{\infty}^{i}<1,\\ (iv)&\mu\text{ is a $C^{1}$-function such that }\|\mu\|\_{\sup}<\infty\text{ and }\lim\_{t\to+\infty}\mu(t)=\mu\_{\infty}\in\mathbb{R}^{d}.\end{array}\right. |  | (2.9) |

Remark:
Under the assumption (ūĚí¶)({\cal K}), főĽif\_{\lambda\_{i}} is a (1‚ąíai)(1-a\_{i})-sum measure, i.e., ‚ąę0+‚ąěfőĽi‚Äč(s)‚ÄčūĚĎĎs=1‚ąíai\int\_{0}^{+\infty}f\_{\lambda\_{i}}(s)\,ds=1-a\_{i}. Furthermore, limt‚Üí+‚ąě‚ąę0tfőĽi‚Äč(t‚ąís)‚Äčőľi‚Äč(s)‚ÄčūĚĎĎs=őľ‚ąěi\lim\_{t\to+\infty}\int\_{0}^{t}f\_{\lambda\_{i}}(t-s)\mu^{i}(s)ds=\mu\_{\infty}^{i} and limt‚Üí+‚ąěŌÜi‚Äč(t)‚ąí(főĽi‚ąóŌÜi)‚Äč(t)=ŌÜ‚ąěi‚Äčai.\lim\_{t\to+\infty}\varphi^{i}(t)-(f\_{\lambda\_{i}}\*\varphi^{i})(t)=\varphi\_{\infty}^{i}\,a\_{i}. (see (Gnabeyeu and Pag√®s, [2025](#bib.bib15), Lemma 3.1)).
Finally, if főĽi=‚ąíRőĽi‚Ä≤>0‚Äč¬†for¬†‚Äčt>0f\_{\lambda\_{i}}=-R^{\prime}\_{\lambda\_{i}}>0\text{ for }t>0, then főĽif\_{\lambda\_{i}} is a probability density in which case, RőĽiR\_{\lambda\_{i}} is non-increasing.
This is in particular the case for the Mittag-Leffler density function főĪi,őĽif\_{\alpha\_{i},\lambda\_{i}} for őĪi‚ąą(12,1)\alpha\_{i}\in(\frac{1}{2},1), in which case főĪi,őĽif\_{\alpha\_{i},\lambda\_{i}} is a completely monotonic function (hence convex), decreasing to 0 while 1‚ąíRőĪi,őĽi1-R\_{\alpha\_{i},\lambda\_{i}} is a Bernstein function (see e.g. (Gnabeyeu and Pag√®s, [2025](#bib.bib15), Proposition 6.1)).
The Proposition below shows what are the consequences of the three constraints in equation ([2.6](#S2.E6 "In Definition 2.2 (Fake Stationarity Regimes). ‚Ä£ 2.1 Stabilizer and fake stationarity regimes. ‚Ä£ 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")).

###### Proposition 2.4 (Fake stationary Volterra square root process.).

Let (Vt)t‚Č•0(V\_{t})\_{t\geq 0} be a solution to the scaled Volterra square root equation in its form ([2.2](#S2.E2 "In 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) starting from any random variable V0‚ąąL2‚Äč(ő©,‚ĄĪ,‚Ąô)V\_{0}\in L^{2}(\Omega,\mathcal{F},\mathbb{P}).
Then, a necessary and sufficient condition for the relations ([2.6](#S2.E6 "In Definition 2.2 (Fake Stationarity Regimes). ‚Ä£ 2.1 Stabilizer and fake stationarity regimes. ‚Ä£ 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) to be satisfied is that for i=1,‚Ä¶,di=1,\ldots,d

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | ūĚĒľ‚Äč[V0i]=1‚ąíai1‚ąíai‚ÄčŌÜ‚ąěi‚Äčőľ‚ąěiőĽi:=x‚ąěi‚Äčand‚Äč‚ąÄt‚Č•0,ŌÜi‚Äč(t)=1‚ąíőĽi‚Äč‚ąę0tKi‚Äč(t‚ąís)‚Äč(őľi‚Äč(s)őĽi‚Äčx‚ąěi‚ąí1)‚Äčds.\displaystyle\ \mathbb{E}[V\_{0}^{i}]=\frac{1-a\_{i}}{1-a\_{i}\varphi\_{\infty}^{i}}\frac{\mu\_{\infty}^{i}}{\lambda\_{i}}:=x\_{\infty}^{i}\qquad\text{and}\qquad\forall\,t\geq 0,\qquad\varphi^{i}(t)=1-\lambda\_{i}\int\_{0}^{t}K\_{i}(t-s)\left(\frac{\mu^{i}(s)}{\lambda\_{i}x\_{\infty}^{i}}-1\right)\,\,\mathrm{d}s. |  | (2.10) |
|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | so that ([2.2](#S2.E2 "In 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) reads:‚ÄčVti=V0i‚ąí1őĽi‚Äčx‚ąěi‚Äč(V0i‚ąíx‚ąěi)‚Äč‚ąę0tfőĽi‚Äč(t‚ąís)‚Äčőľi‚Äč(s)‚Äčds+1őĽi‚Äč‚ąę0tfőĽi‚Äč(t‚ąís)‚ÄčŌāi‚Äč(s)‚ÄčVsi‚ÄčūĚĎĎWsi.\displaystyle\text{so that\penalty 10000\ \eqref{VolSqrt\_} reads:}\;V\_{t}^{i}=V\_{0}^{i}-\frac{1}{\lambda\_{i}x\_{\infty}^{i}}\Big(V\_{0}^{i}-x\_{\infty}^{i}\Big)\int\_{0}^{t}f\_{\lambda\_{i}}(t-s)\mu^{i}(s)\,\mathrm{d}s+\frac{1}{\lambda\_{i}}\int\_{0}^{t}f\_{\lambda\_{i}}(t-s)\varsigma^{i}(s)\sqrt{V^{i}\_{s}}dW^{i}\_{s}. |  | (2.11) |

and the couple (v0i,Ōāi‚Äč(t))(v\_{0}^{i},\varsigma^{i}(t)), where v0i=Var‚Äč(V0i)v\_{0}^{i}=\text{Var}(V\_{0}^{i}) must satisfy the functional equation:

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | (EőĽi,ci):‚ąÄt‚Č•0,ci‚ÄčőĽi2‚Äč(1‚ąí(ŌÜi‚Äč(t)‚ąí(főĽi‚ąóŌÜi)t)2)=(főĽi2‚ąóŌāi‚Äč2)‚Äč(t)‚Äčwhere‚Äčci=v0iőĹi2‚Äčx‚ąěi‚Äči.e.‚ÄčŌāi=ŌāőĽi,cii.\textit{($E\_{\lambda\_{i},c\_{i}}$)}:\;\forall\,t\geq 0,\;c\_{i}\lambda\_{i}^{2}\big(1-(\varphi^{i}(t)-(f\_{\lambda\_{i}}\*\varphi^{i})\_{t})^{2}\big)=(f\_{\lambda\_{i}}^{2}\*\varsigma^{i2})(t)\;\textit{where}\;c\_{i}=\frac{v\_{0}^{i}}{\nu\_{i}^{2}x\_{\infty}^{i}}\;\textit{i.e.}\;\varsigma^{i}=\varsigma^{i}\_{\lambda\_{i},c\_{i}}. |  | (2.12) |

Proof : This is a straightforward extension to the multi-dimensional setting of (Gnabeyeu and Pag√®s, [2025](#bib.bib15), Proposition 3.4 and Theorem 3.5) (see also (Gnabeyeu et al., [a](#bib.bib16), Proposition 4.2 and 4.4)).

###### Definition 2.5.

We will call the stabilizer (or corrector) of the scaled stochastic Volterra equation ([2.2](#S2.E2 "In 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) the (locally) bounded Borel function Ōā=diag‚Ā°(Ōā1,‚Ä¶,Ōād)\varsigma=\operatorname{diag}(\varsigma^{1},\ldots,\varsigma^{d}) where Ōāi\varsigma^{i} is a solution(if any) to the functional equation (EőĽi,ciE\_{\lambda\_{i},c\_{i}}) in ([2.12](#S2.E12 "In Proposition 2.4 (Fake stationary Volterra square root process.). ‚Ä£ 2.1 Stabilizer and fake stationarity regimes. ‚Ä£ 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) for i=1,‚Ä¶,di=1,\ldots,d.

###### Example 2.6.

### 2.2 Formulation of the stochastic Market model

We consider a financial market on [0,T][0,T] on some filtered probability space (ő©,‚ĄĪ,ūĚĒĹ:=(‚ĄĪt)t‚Č•0,‚Ąô)(\Omega,{\mathcal{F}},\mathbb{F}:=({\mathcal{F}}\_{t})\_{t\geq 0},\mathbb{P}) with d+1d+1 securities, consisting of a bond and dd stocks. The non‚Äďrisky asset S0S^{0} satisfies the (stochastic) ordinary differential equation:

|  | d‚ÄčSt0=St0‚Äčr‚Äč(t)‚Äčd‚Äčt,\displaystyle dS^{0}\_{t}=S^{0}\_{t}r(t)dt, |  |

with a time-dependent deterministic short risk-free rate r:‚ĄĚ+‚Üí‚ĄĚr:\mathbb{R}\_{+}\to\mathbb{R}, and dd risky assets (stock or index) whose return vector process (St)t‚Č•0=(St1,‚Ä¶,Std)t‚Č•0(S\_{t})\_{t\geq 0}=(S\_{t}^{1},\ldots,S\_{t}^{d})\_{t\geq 0} is defined via the dynamics given by the vector-stochastic differential equation (SDE):

and a ‚ĄĚd\mathbb{R}^{d}-valued continuous stochastic process őĽ\lambda,
called market price of risk. Here ūĚüôd{\mathbb{1}\_{d}} denotes the vector in ‚ĄĚd\mathbb{R}^{d} with all components equal to 11 and the correlation structure of WW with BB is given by

for some (ŌĀ1,‚Ä¶,ŌĀd)‚ąą[‚ąí1,1]d(\rho\_{1},\ldots,\rho\_{d})\in[-1,1]^{d},

The correlation ŌĀi\rho\_{i} between stock price SiS^{i} and variance ViV^{i} is assumed constant.
Note that d‚Äč‚ü®Wi‚ü©t=d‚Äčtd\langle W^{i}\rangle\_{t}=dt but WiW^{i} and WjW^{j} can be correlated, hence WW is not necessarily a Brownian motion.

Observe that
processes őĽ\lambda and ŌÉ\sigma are ūĚĒĹ\mathbb{F}-adapted, possibly unbounded, but not necessarily adapted to the filtration generated by WW. We point out that ūĚĒĹ\mathbb{F} may be strictly larger than the augmented filtration generated by BB and B‚üāB^{\perp} as we deal with weak solutions to stochastic Volterra equations.

We assume that ŌÉ\sigma in ([2.14](#S2.E14 "In 2.2 Formulation of the stochastic Market model ‚Ä£ 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) is given by ŌÉ=diag‚Ā°(V)\sigma=\sqrt{\operatorname{diag}(V)}, where the ‚ĄĚ+d\mathbb{R}^{d}\_{+}‚Äďvalued scaled process VV is defined in ([2.2](#S2.E2 "In 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) with Ōā=ŌāD,c\varsigma=\varsigma\_{D,c} and Equation ([2.10](#S2.E10 "In Proposition 2.4 (Fake stationary Volterra square root process.). ‚Ä£ 2.1 Stabilizer and fake stationarity regimes. ‚Ä£ 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) holds true. We will be chiefly interested in the case where őĽt\lambda\_{t} is linear
in ŌÉt\sigma\_{t}. More specifically, the the market price of risk (risk premium) is assumed to be in the form
őĽ\lambda == (őł1‚ÄčV1,‚Ä¶,őłd‚ÄčVd)‚ä§\big(\theta\_{1}\sqrt{V^{1}},\ldots,\theta\_{d}\sqrt{V^{d}}\big)^{\top}, for some constant őłi‚Č•0\theta\_{i}\geq 0, so that the dynamics for the stock prices ([2.14](#S2.E14 "In 2.2 Formulation of the stochastic Market model ‚Ä£ 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) reads following Kraft ([2005](#bib.bib25)); Abi Jaber et al. Since SS is fully determined by VV, the existence of SS readily follows from that of VV. In particular, weak existence of H√∂lder pathwise continuous solution VV of ([2.2](#S2.E2 "In 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) such that ([2.5](#S2.E5 "In 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) holds is established under suitable assumptions on the kernel KK and specifications g0g\_{0} as shown in the following remark.

We state the following existence and uniqueness result from Gnabeyeu et al. ([b](#bib.bib17)) which is extended to the multi-dimensional setting.

((Gnabeyeu et al., [b](#bib.bib17), Theorem 3.1 and Remark on Theorem 3.2)). |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | supt‚Č§TūĚĒľ‚Äč[‚ÄĖVt‚ÄĖp]<‚ąě,p>0.\displaystyle\sup\_{t\leq T}\mathbb{E}\left[\|V\_{t}\|^{p}\right]<\infty,\quad p>0. |  | (2.17) |

From now on, we set g0‚Äč(t):=ŌÜ‚Äč(t)‚ÄčV0+‚ąę0tK‚Äč(t‚ąís)‚Äčőľ‚Äč(s)‚ÄčūĚĎĎsg\_{0}(t):=\varphi(t)V\_{0}+\int\_{0}^{t}K(t-s)\mu(s)ds and d‚ÄčZt=D‚ÄčVt‚Äčd‚Äčt+őĹ‚Äčdiag‚Ā°(Vt)‚Äčd‚ÄčWt,‚ąÄt‚Č•0dZ\_{t}=DV\_{t}dt+\nu\sqrt{\operatorname{diag}(V\_{t})}dW\_{t},\;\forall t\geq 0 so that Equation ([2.2](#S2.E2 "In 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) reads

|  |  |  |  |

|  | Vt=g0‚Äč(t)+‚ąę0tK‚Äč(t‚ąís)‚ÄčD‚ÄčVs‚ÄčūĚĎĎs+‚ąę0tK‚Äč(t‚ąís)‚ÄčőĹ‚ÄčŌā‚Äč(s)‚Äčdiag‚Ā°(Vs)‚ÄčūĚĎĎWs=g0‚Äč(t)+‚ąę0tK‚Äč(t‚ąís)‚ÄčūĚĎĎZs.\displaystyle V\_{t}=g\_{0}(t)+\int\_{0}^{t}K(t-s)DV\_{s}ds+\int\_{0}^{t}K(t-s)\nu\varsigma(s)\sqrt{\operatorname{diag}(V\_{s})}dW\_{s}=g\_{0}(t)+\int\_{0}^{t}K(t-s)dZ\_{s}. |  | (2.18) |

One notes that for each, s‚Č§Ts\leq T, (gt‚Äč(s))t‚Č§s(g\_{t}(s))\_{t\leq s} is the adjusted forward process

| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |

This adjusted forward process is commonly used (see, e.g., Abi Jaber et al. ([2021](#bib.bib2))) to elucidate the affine structure of affine Volterra processes with continuous trajectories.
  
The process in ([2.18](#S2.E18 "In 2.2 Formulation of the stochastic Market model ‚Ä£ 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) is non-Markovian and non-semimartingale in general. Note that our model ([2.16](#S2.E16 "In 2.2 Formulation of the stochastic Market model ‚Ä£ 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models"))-([2.15](#S2.E15 "In 2.2 Formulation of the stochastic Market model ‚Ä£ 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models"))-([2.2](#S2.E2 "In 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) features correlation between the stocks and between a stock and its volatility. Moreover, the methodology developed in this paper, and hence the results obtained, remain valid if the matrix DD in ([2.2](#S2.E2 "In 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) is not assumed to be diagonal, but only satisfies

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | D‚ąą‚ĄĚd√ód,Di‚Äčj‚Č•0‚Äčfor¬†‚Äči‚Č†j.D\in\mathbb{R}^{d\times d},\qquad D\_{ij}\geq 0\ \text{for }i\neq j. |  |

This also provides an extension to the inhomogeneous setting of the models considered in Abi Jaber et al. ([2019](#bib.bib1), [2021](#bib.bib2)); Aichinger and Desmettre ([2021](#bib.bib3)).

## 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation

‚ä≥\rhd Preliminaries and Problem formulation: As we deal with weak solutions to stochastic Volterra equations ([2.16](#S2.E16 "In 2.2 Formulation of the stochastic Market model ‚Ä£ 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models"))-([2.2](#S2.E2 "In 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")), Brownian motion is also a part of the solution. However, expected utility only depends on the expectation of the wealth process. In the sequel, we fix a version of the solution (S,V,B,B‚ä§)(S,V,B,B^{\top}) to ([2.16](#S2.E16 "In 2.2 Formulation of the stochastic Market model ‚Ä£ 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models"))-([2.2](#S2.E2 "In 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) as other solutions have the same law.

We consider the classical problem of maximizing the expected utility of terminal wealth. A portfolio strategy őĪt=(őĪt,1,‚Ä¶,őĪt,d)‚ä§\alpha\_{t}=(\alpha\_{t,1},\ldots,\alpha\_{t,d})^{\top} is an ‚ĄĚd\mathbb{R}^{d}-valued, ūĚĒĹ\mathbb{F}-progressively measurable process, where őĪt,k\alpha\_{t,k} represents the proportion of wealth invested in asset kk at time tt. Under a fixed portfolio strategy, the corresponding wealth process (XtőĪ)t‚Č•0(X\_{t}^{\alpha})\_{t\geq 0} depend on VV in ([2.2](#S2.E2 "In 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) and has a certain dynamic to be specified latter.
By ūĚíú\mathcal{A} we denote the set of admissible portfolio or investment strategies i.e. the set of all ūĚĒĹ\mathbb{F}-progressively measurable processes (őĪt)t‚ąą[0,T](\alpha\_{t})\_{t\in[0,T]} valued in the Polish space ‚ĄĚd\mathbb{R}^{d}.

To ease notation burden, whenever the context is clear, we simply write XX, instead of XőĪX^{\alpha}, as the wealth process under őĪ‚ąąūĚíú\alpha\in{\mathcal{A}} with initial condition X0=x0>0X\_{0}=x\_{0}>0 and V0>0V\_{0}>0.

###### Definition 3.1.

1. 1.

   A utility function is a strictly increasing and strictly concave function U:(0,‚ąě)‚Üí‚ĄĚ‚ą™{‚ąí‚ąě},U:(0,\infty)\to\mathbb{R}\cup\{-\infty\},
   which is continuously differentiable on (0,‚ąě)(0,\infty).

   In the following, UU denotes a general utility function. Later, we will focus on power utility functions of the form U‚Äč(x)=xő≥ő≥,for¬†‚Äčő≥‚ąą‚ĄĚ+‚ąĖ{0,1},U(x)=\frac{x^{\gamma}}{\gamma},\;\text{for }\gamma\in\mathbb{R}\_{+}\setminus\{0,1\},
   or alternatively on exponential utility functions of the form U‚Äč(x)=‚ąí1ő≥‚Äče‚ąíő≥‚Äčx,for¬†‚Äčő≥>0.U(x)=-\frac{1}{\gamma}e^{-\gamma x},\;\text{for }\gamma>0. ő≥\gamma is typically called the risk aversion parameter.
2. 2.

   An admissible strategy őĪ‚ąąūĚíú\alpha\in\mathcal{A} is said to be optimal (for terminal wealth) if it maximizes őĪ‚üľūĚĒľ‚Äč[U‚Äč(XTőĪ)]\alpha\longmapsto\mathbb{E}\big[U(X\_{T}^{\alpha})\big]
   over all admissible strategies in ūĚíú\mathcal{A}. That is the portfolio strategy őĪ‚ąó\alpha^{\*} for which the supremum is attained

The investor‚Äôs goal in the Merton problem is to find an optimal strategy so as to maximize the expected utility of terminal wealth. Specifically, given the utility function UU on (0,‚ąě)(0,\infty) and starting from an initial capital x0>0x\_{0}>0,
the objective of the agent is

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | ūĚíĪ‚Äč(x0,V0):=supőĪ‚Äč(‚čÖ)‚ąąūĚíúūĚĒľ‚Äč[U‚Äč(XTőĪ)],given‚Äčx0‚Äčand‚ÄčV0.\mathcal{V}(x\_{0},V\_{0}):=\sup\_{\alpha(\cdot)\in\mathcal{A}}\mathbb{E}\!\left[U\!\left(X\_{T}^{\alpha}\right)\right],\;\text{given}\;x\_{0}\;\text{and}\;V\_{0}. |  | (3.21) |

with XőĪX^{\alpha} the wealth
controlled by őĪ‚ąąūĚíú\alpha\in\mathcal{A}, starting from x0x\_{0} at time 0
and ūĚíú\mathcal{A} the subset of controls őĪ‚ąąūĚíú\alpha\in\mathcal{A} such that the family {U‚Äč(XŌĄőĪ):ŌĄ‚ąą[0,T]}\left\{U\!\left(X\_{\tau}^{\alpha}\right):\tau\in[0,T]\right\}
is uniformly integrable.
The preferences of the agent are thus described by the utility function UU.
Mathematically, we aim at identifying the optimal value associated with the utility maximization problem defined over a finite horizon TT by

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | ūĚíĪt‚Äč(x,v):=ess‚ÄčsupőĪ‚ąąūĚíút‚Ā°ūĚĒľx,v‚Äč[U‚Äč(XTt,x,v,őĪ)‚ą£‚ĄĪt],x>0,v>0,t‚ąą[0,T],\mathcal{V}\_{t}(x,v):=\operatorname\*{ess\,sup}\_{\alpha\in\mathcal{A}\_{t}}\mathbb{E}\_{x,v}\!\left[U\!\left(X\_{T}^{t,x,v,\alpha}\right)\mid\mathcal{F}\_{t}\right],\qquad x>0,v>0,\;t\in[0,T], |  | (3.22) |

and the optimal strategy őĪ‚ąó\alpha^{\ast}, given the preference described by the utility function U‚Äč(‚čÖ)U(\cdot).
This is a standard stochastic control problem. The set ūĚíút\mathcal{A}\_{t} is the class of all admissible strategies from t
with zero being an absorbing state for XtőĪX\_{t}^{\alpha} (bankruptcy).
Here ūĚĒľx,v\mathbb{E}\_{x,v} denotes expectation under the conditional distribution given Xt=xX\_{t}=x and Vt=vV\_{t}=v, and where the supremum is taken over all admissible portfolio strategies.

The ūĚĒĹ\mathbb{F}-adapted process {ūĚíĪt,‚ÄČ0‚Č§t‚Č§T}\{\mathcal{V}\_{t},\,0\leq t\leq T\}
is a supermartingale.
Moreover, there exists an optimal control őĪ‚ąó‚ąąūĚíú\alpha^{\*}\in\mathcal{A} for ([3.21](#S3.E21 "In 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models"))
if and only if the martingale property holds, that is,
the process {ūĚíĪt‚ąó,‚ÄČ0‚Č§t‚Č§T}\{\mathcal{V}^{\*}\_{t},\,0\leq t\leq T\} for őĪ‚ąó\alpha^{\*} is a martingale.
The idea is that an admissible control (or startegy) is optimal333optimal strategy: No expected gain from deviation, this implies martingality if the associated value process is a martingale and for any other admissible control, it is a supermartingale. That is the classic martingale optimality principle, see, e.g., Hu et al. ([2005](#bib.bib21)), Pham ([2009](#bib.bib28), Section 6.6.1) or Jeanblanc et al. ([2012](#bib.bib22)).

###### Definition 3.2 (Martingale optimality principle).

The Problem ([3.21](#S3.E21 "In 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) can be solved by constructing a family of processes {JtőĪ}t‚ąą[0,T]\{J^{\alpha}\_{t}\}\_{t\in[0,T]}, őĪ‚ąąūĚíú\alpha\in{\mathcal{A}}, satisfying the conditions:

1. 1.

   JTőĪ=U‚Äč(XT)J^{\alpha}\_{T}=U(X\_{T}) for all őĪ‚ąąūĚíú\alpha\in{\mathcal{A}};
2. 2.

   J0őĪJ^{\alpha}\_{0} is a constant, independent of őĪ‚ąąūĚíú\alpha\in{\mathcal{A}};
3. 3.

   JtőĪJ^{\alpha}\_{t} is a supermartingale for all őĪ‚ąąūĚíú\alpha\in{\mathcal{A}}, and there exists őĪ‚ąó‚ąąūĚíú\alpha^{\*}\in{\mathcal{A}} such that JőĪ‚ąóJ^{\alpha^{\*}} is a martingale.

A family of processes with the above properties can now be used to compare the expected utilities of an arbitrary strategy őĪ‚ąąūĚíú\alpha\in{\mathcal{A}} and the strategy őĪ‚ąó\alpha^{\*}:

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | ūĚĒľ‚Äč[U‚Äč(XTőĪ)]=ūĚĒľ‚Äč[JTőĪ]‚Č§J0őĪ=J0őĪ‚ąó=ūĚĒľ‚Äč[JTőĪ‚ąó]=ūĚĒľ‚Äč[U‚Äč(XTőĪ‚ąó)]=ūĚíĪ‚Äč(x0,V0).\mathbb{E}[U(X\_{T}^{\alpha})]=\mathbb{E}[J^{\alpha}\_{T}]\leq J^{\alpha}\_{0}=J^{\alpha^{\*}}\_{0}=\mathbb{E}[J^{\alpha^{\*}}\_{T}]=\mathbb{E}[U(X^{\alpha^{\*}}\_{T})]=\mathcal{V}(x\_{0},V\_{0}). |  |

where XőĪ‚ąóX^{\alpha^{\*}} is the wealth process under őĪ‚ąó\alpha^{\*}. Thus the strategy őĪ‚ąó\alpha^{\*} is indeed our desired optimal portfolio strategy.

As stated before, Problem ([3.21](#S3.E21 "In 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) seen as an optimization problem with state process XőĪX^{\alpha} is non-Markovian and the standard stochastic control approach cannot be applied.
Heuristically speaking, the non-Markovian and non-semimartingale
characteristics of the multivariate fake stationary Volterra Heston model ([2.16](#S2.E16 "In 2.2 Formulation of the stochastic Market model ‚Ä£ 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models"))-([2.2](#S2.E2 "In 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) are overcome in the degenerate correlation case by applying the martingale optimality principle
and constructing an ansatz, which is inspired by the martingale distortion transformation and the exponential-affine representation (see e.g. (Gnabeyeu, [2026](#bib.bib14), Theorem A.4.)) in term of an auxiliary process denoted őď‚Č°őď‚Äč(Vt)\Gamma\equiv\Gamma(V\_{t}) (more precisely őď‚Äč(gt)\Gamma(g\_{t})).
In the general correlation case, we provide a verification argument avoiding restrictions on the correlation structure linked to the martingale distortion transformation.

In fact, Fouque and Hu ([2019](#bib.bib12)) showed that if the Sharpe-ratio őĽ\lambda in [2.14](#S2.E14 "In 2.2 Formulation of the stochastic Market model ‚Ä£ 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models") is bounded and has bounded derivative, then the value process ūĚíĪt\mathcal{V}\_{t} can be expressed as ūĚíĪt‚Äč(x,v)=Jt‚Äč(XtőĪ=x,Vt=v)\mathcal{V}\_{t}(x,v)=J\_{t}(X\_{t}^{\alpha}=x,V\_{t}=v), where

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | Jt‚Äč(XtőĪ,Vt):=F‚Äč(t,XtőĪ)‚Äčőď‚Äč(Vt)J\_{t}(X\_{t}^{\alpha},V\_{t}):=F(t,X\_{t}^{\alpha})\Gamma(V\_{t}) |  | (3.23) |

for the power utility case (F‚Äč(t,XtőĪ)=U‚Äč(XtőĪ)=(XtőĪ)ő≥ő≥F(t,X\_{t}^{\alpha})=U(X\_{t}^{\alpha})=\frac{(X\_{t}^{\alpha})^{\gamma}}{\gamma}) even if the volatility process VtV\_{t} is non-Markovian.
This approach is called the martingale distortion transformation and was first introduced in the seminal paper Zariphopoulou ([2001](#bib.bib34)) and later transferred to a non-Markovian setting with H√∂lder-type inequalities in Tehranchi ([2004](#bib.bib30)) for both power utility and exponential utility case (in which F‚Äč(t,XtőĪ)=‚ąí1ő≥‚Äčexp‚Ā°(‚ąíő≥‚Äče‚ąętTr‚Äč(s)‚ÄčūĚĎĎs‚ÄčXtőĪ)F(t,X\_{t}^{\alpha})=-\frac{1}{\gamma}\exp\Big(-\gamma e^{\int^{T}\_{t}r(s)ds}X\_{t}^{\alpha}\Big)). The extension to the multi-asset case is straight forward in the case of a bounded risk premium and degenerate correlation structure(cf. Fouque and Hu ([2019](#bib.bib12)), Remark 2.5.).

We will provide concrete specifications of the process őď\Gamma depending on the problem at hand.
The semi-closed form exponential‚Äďaffine representation (Gnabeyeu, [2026](#bib.bib14), Theorem A.4.) of the functional őď\Gamma can be expressed in terms of the continuous solution Ōą\psi
of an associated time-inhomogeneous Riccati-type Volterra equation, which can be solved by well-known efficient numerical methods.

Note that, in contrast to Han and Wong ([2020](#bib.bib19)); Aichinger and Desmettre ([2021](#bib.bib3)), this representation is expressed in terms of the adjusted forward process, as defined in ([2.19](#S2.E19 "In 2.2 Formulation of the stochastic Market model ‚Ä£ 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models"))‚Äď([2.20](#S2.E20 "In 2.2 Formulation of the stochastic Market model ‚Ä£ 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")), rather than the forward process used in these works.
We offer explicit solutions to the optimal portfolio policies that depend on the function Ōą\psi, solution of the above-mentionned time-dependent multivariate Riccati-Volterra equation.
Let őõ\Lambda be defined as

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | őõti=őĹi‚ÄčŌāi‚Äč(t)‚ÄčŌąi‚Äč(T‚ąít)‚ÄčVti,i=1,‚Ä¶,d,0‚Č§t‚Č§T,\Lambda\_{t}^{i}=\nu\_{i}\varsigma^{i}(t)\psi^{i}(T-t)\sqrt{V^{i}\_{t}},\quad i=1,\ldots,d,\quad 0\leq t\leq T, |  | (3.24) |

We will work under the following assumption,

###### Assumption 3.1.

Assume that there exists a solution
Ōą‚ąąC‚Äč([0,T],‚ĄĚd)\psi\in C([0,T],\mathbb{R}^{d}) to the above-mentioned inhomogeneous Riccati‚ÄďVolterra equation satisfying the below appropriate
boundedness condition i.e. such that

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | max1‚Č§i‚Č§d‚Äčsupt‚ąą[0,T](őłi2+őĹi2‚ÄčŌāi‚Äč(t)2‚ÄčŌąi‚Äč(T‚ąít)2)‚Č§aa‚Äč(p),\max\_{1\leq i\leq d}\sup\_{t\in[0,T]}\left(\theta\_{i}^{2}+\nu\_{i}^{2}\varsigma^{i}(t)^{2}\psi^{i}(T-t)^{2}\right)\leq\frac{a}{a(p)}, |  | (3.25) |

holds for a sufficient large p>1p>1, where the constant a‚Äč(p)a(p) is given by

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |

and the constant a>0a>0 is such that ūĚĒľ‚Äč[exp‚Ā°(a‚Äč‚ąę0T‚ąĎi=1dVsi‚Äčd‚Äčs)]<‚ąě\mathbb{E}\left[\exp\big(a\int\_{0}^{T}\sum\_{i=1}^{d}V^{i}\_{s}ds\big)\right]<\infty.

Remark on Assumption [3.1](#S3.Thmassumption1 "Assumption 3.1. ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models"): Note that if Assumption [3.1](#S3.Thmassumption1 "Assumption 3.1. ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models") hold, then

|  |  |  |  |

|  | ūĚĒľ‚Äč[exp‚Ā°(a‚Äč(p)‚Äč‚ąę0T(|őĽs|2+|őõs|2)‚ÄčūĚĎĎs)]<‚ąě,\mathbb{E}\Big[\exp\Big(a(p)\int\_{0}^{T}\big(|\lambda\_{s}|^{2}+\left|\Lambda\_{s}\right|^{2}\big)ds\Big)\Big]\;<\;\infty, |  | (3.27) |

holds for some p>1p>1 and a constant a‚Äč(p)a(p) given by ([3.26](#S3.E26 "In Assumption 3.1. ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")).

In fact, under Assumption [3.1](#S3.Thmassumption1 "Assumption 3.1. ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models"), we will have

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | a‚Äč(p)‚Äč(|őĽs|2+|őõs|2)=a‚Äč(p)‚Äč‚ąĎi=1dVsi‚Äč(őłi2+őĹi2‚ÄčŌāi‚Äč(s)2‚ÄčŌąi‚Äč(T‚ąís)2)‚Č§a‚Äč‚ąĎi=1dVsi,a(p)\left(|\lambda\_{s}|^{2}+\left|\Lambda\_{s}\right|^{2}\right)\;=\;a(p)\sum\_{i=1}^{d}V\_{s}^{i}\left(\theta\_{i}^{2}+\nu\_{i}^{2}\varsigma^{i}(s)^{2}\psi^{i}(T-s)^{2}\right)\;\leq\;a\sum\_{i=1}^{d}V\_{s}^{i}, |  | (3.28) |

which implies that ūĚĒľ‚Äč[exp‚Ā°(a‚Äč(p)‚Äč‚ąę0T(|őĽs|2+|őõs|2)‚ÄčūĚĎĎs)]<‚ąě\mathbb{E}\left[\exp\left(a(p)\int\_{0}^{T}\left(|\lambda\_{s}|^{2}+\left|\Lambda\_{s}\right|^{2}\right)ds\right)\right]<\infty.

Remark:
Condition ([3.25](#S3.E25 "In Assumption 3.1. ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) concerns the risk premium constants (őł1,‚Ä¶,őłd)(\theta\_{1},\ldots,\theta\_{d}). For a large enough constant a>0a>0, from (Gnabeyeu, [2026](#bib.bib14), Theorem A.4.) ( with ‚Ą≥‚ąčm‚Äč(d‚Äčs):=a‚ÄčūĚüôd‚Äčőī0‚Äč(d‚Äčs)\mathcal{M}\ni m(\,\mathrm{d}s):=a{\mathbb{1}\_{d}}\,\delta\_{0}(\,\mathrm{d}s)), a sufficient condition ensuring

|  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | Ōą~i‚Äč(t)\displaystyle\tilde{\psi}^{i}(t) | =‚ąę0tKi‚Äč(t‚ąís)‚Äč(a+(D‚ä§‚ÄčŌą~‚Äč(s))i+őĹi22‚Äč(Ōāi‚Äč(T‚ąís)‚ÄčŌą~i‚Äč(s))2)‚ÄčūĚĎĎs,i=1,‚Ä¶,d,‚ÄĄ‚ÄĄ0‚Č§t‚Č§T.\displaystyle=\;\int\_{0}^{t}K\_{i}(t-s)\Big(a+\big(D^{\top}\tilde{\psi}(s)\big)\_{i}+\frac{\nu\_{i}^{2}}{2}(\varsigma^{i}(T-s)\tilde{\psi}^{i}(s))^{2}\Big)ds,\;\;i=1,\ldots,d,\;\;0\leq t\leq T. |  | (3.29) |

Power and exponential utility functions are widely adopted in the literature and display distinct risk-aversion properties. Specifically, the power utility function exhibits constant relative risk aversion (CRRA),
whereas the exponential utility function is characterized by constant absolute risk aversion (CARA). Optimal strategies corresponding to these utility functions are presented in the sequel, within the framework of the model introduced in Section [2](#S2 "2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models").

### 3.1 Optimal strategy for the power utility maximization problem

Here, we denote by ŌÄt\pi\_{t} the proportion of wealth invested in the risky assets SS.
An agent invests at any time tt the proportion ŌÄt\pi\_{t} of his wealth XtŌÄX^{\pi}\_{t} in the stocks SS
of price‚Äôs vector StS\_{t}, and the remaining proportion 1‚ąíŌÄt‚ä§‚ÄčūĚüôd1-\pi\_{t}^{\top}{\mathbb{1}\_{d}} in a bond of price St0S\_{t}^{0}
with interest rate r‚Äč(t)r(t). The notation XtŌÄX^{\pi}\_{t} emphasizes the dependence of the wealth on the strategy ŌÄ=(ŌÄt)t‚Č•0\pi=(\pi\_{t})\_{t\geq 0}.
The portfolio strategy ŌÄt=(ŌÄt1,‚Ä¶,ŌÄtd)\pi\_{t}=(\pi\_{t}^{1},\dots,\pi\_{t}^{d}) is an (‚ĄĚd)‚ąó(\mathbb{R}^{d})^{\*} valued, progressively measurable process, where ŌÄtk\pi\_{t}^{k} represents the proportion of wealth invested into stock kk at time tt.
Assuming the model ([2.14](#S2.E14 "In 2.2 Formulation of the stochastic Market model ‚Ä£ 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models"))‚Äď ([2.16](#S2.E16 "In 2.2 Formulation of the stochastic Market model ‚Ä£ 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) for StS\_{t}, the dynamics of the controlled wealth process is given by

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | d‚ÄčXtŌÄ\displaystyle\mathrm{d}X^{\pi}\_{t} | =XtŌÄ‚Äč(ŌÄt‚ä§‚Äč(r‚Äč(t)‚ÄčūĚüôd+ŌÉ‚Äč(Vt)‚ÄčőĽt)+(1‚ąíŌÄt‚ä§‚ÄčūĚüôd)‚Äčr‚Äč(t))‚Äčd‚Äčt+XtŌÄ‚ÄčŌÄt‚ä§‚ÄčŌÉ‚Äč(Vt)‚Äčd‚ÄčBt\displaystyle=X^{\pi}\_{t}\bigl(\pi\_{t}^{\top}\big(r(t){\mathbb{1}\_{d}}+\sigma(V\_{t})\lambda\_{t}\big)+(1-\pi\_{t}^{\top}{\mathbb{1}\_{d}})r(t)\bigr)\,\mathrm{d}t+X^{\pi}\_{t}\pi\_{t}^{\top}\sigma(V\_{t})\,\mathrm{d}B\_{t} |  |
|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  |  | =XtŌÄ‚Äč(r‚Äč(t)+ŌÄt‚ä§‚ÄčŌÉ‚Äč(Vt)‚ÄčőĽt)‚Äčd‚Äčt+XtŌÄ‚ÄčŌÄt‚ä§‚ÄčŌÉ‚Äč(Vt)‚Äčd‚ÄčBt=XtŌÄ‚Äč(r‚Äč(t)+ŌÄt‚ä§‚Äčdiag‚Ā°(Vt)‚Äčőł)‚Äčd‚Äčt+Xt‚ÄčŌÄt‚ä§‚Äčdiag‚Ā°(Vt)‚Äčd‚ÄčBt,\displaystyle=X^{\pi}\_{t}\bigl(r(t)+\pi\_{t}^{\top}\sigma(V\_{t})\lambda\_{t}\bigr)\,\mathrm{d}t+X^{\pi}\_{t}\pi\_{t}^{\top}\sigma(V\_{t})\,\mathrm{d}B\_{t}=X\_{t}^{\pi}(r(t)+\pi\_{t}^{\top}{\operatorname{diag}(V\_{t})}{\theta})dt+X\_{t}\pi\_{t}^{\top}\sqrt{\operatorname{diag}(V\_{t})}dB\_{t}, |  |

where őł=(őł1,‚Ä¶,őłd)‚ä§{\theta}=(\theta\_{1},\dots,\theta\_{d})^{\top}.
The investor faces the portfolio constraint that, at any time tt,
ŌÄt\pi\_{t} takes values in a closed convex subset ūĚíú‚äā‚ĄĚd\mathcal{A}\subset\mathbb{R}^{d} denoting the set of admissible portfolio strategies.

From now, we let őĪt:=ŌÉ‚Äč(Vt)‚ä§‚ÄčŌÄt\alpha\_{t}:=\sigma(V\_{t})^{\top}\pi\_{t} be the investment strategy. Then, under a fixed portfolio strategy, the wealth process XtőĪX^{\alpha}\_{t}, controlled by őĪ\alpha is governed by:

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | d‚ÄčXtőĪ=(r‚Äč(t)+őĪt‚ä§‚ÄčőĽt)‚ÄčXtőĪ‚Äčd‚Äčt+őĪt‚ä§‚ÄčXtőĪ‚Äčd‚ÄčBt,X0=x0>0.dX^{\alpha}\_{t}=\big(r(t)+\alpha\_{t}^{\top}\lambda\_{t}\big)X^{\alpha}\_{t}dt+\alpha\_{t}^{\top}X^{\alpha}\_{t}dB\_{t},\;X\_{0}=x\_{0}>0. |  | (3.30) |

By solving the linear SDE ([3.30](#S3.E30 "In 3.1 Optimal strategy for the power utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")), the wealth process admits the explicit representation

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | XtőĪ=x0‚Äčexp‚Ā°(‚ąę0t(r‚Äč(s)+őĪs‚ä§‚ÄčőĽs‚ąí12‚Äč|őĪs|2)‚ÄčūĚĎĎs+‚ąę0tőĪs‚ä§‚ÄčūĚĎĎBs),x0‚Č•0.X\_{t}^{\alpha}=x\_{0}\exp\!\left(\int\_{0}^{t}\Big(r(s)+\alpha\_{s}^{\top}\lambda\_{s}-\tfrac{1}{2}\left|\alpha\_{s}\right|^{2}\Big)\,ds+\int\_{0}^{t}\alpha\_{s}^{\top}\,dB\_{s}\right),\quad x\_{0}\geq 0. |  | (3.31) |

By a solution to ([3.30](#S3.E30 "In 3.1 Optimal strategy for the power utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")), we mean an ūĚĒĹ\mathbb{F}-adapted process XőĪX^{\alpha} satisfying ([3.30](#S3.E30 "In 3.1 Optimal strategy for the power utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) on [0,T][0,T] with ‚Ąô\mathbb{P}-a.s. continuous sample paths and such that

|  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | ūĚĒľ‚Äč[supt‚Č§T|XtőĪ|p]\displaystyle\mathbb{E}\big[\sup\_{t\leq T}|X^{\alpha}\_{t}|^{p}\big] | <‚ąěfor some¬†p>1.\displaystyle<\;\infty\quad\text{for some }\quad p>1. |  | (3.32) |

The conditions under which we consider a strategy to be admissible is specified in the below definition.

###### Definition 3.3.

In the setting described above, we say that an investment strategy őĪ‚Äč(‚čÖ)\alpha(\cdot) is admissible if

1. (a)(a)

   The SDE ([3.30](#S3.E30 "In 3.1 Optimal strategy for the power utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) for the wealth process (XtőĪ)(X\_{t}^{\alpha}) has a unique solution in terms of (S,V,B)(S,V,B); with ‚Ąô\mathbb{P}-a.s. continuous paths and Xt‚Č•0X\_{t}\geq 0, ‚ąÄt‚ąą[0,T]\forall\;t\in[0,T], ‚Ąô\mathbb{P}-a.s.;
2. (b)(b)

   ūĚĒľ‚Äč[1ő≥‚Äč(XTőĪ)ő≥]<‚ąě\mathbb{E}[\frac{1}{\gamma}(X\_{T}^{\alpha})^{\gamma}]<\infty for all 0<ő≥<10<\gamma<1;
3. (c)(c)

   őĪ‚Äč(‚čÖ)\alpha(\cdot) is ūĚĒĹ\mathbb{F}-adapted and ‚ąę0T|őĪs|2‚ÄčūĚĎĎs<‚ąě\int^{T}\_{0}\left|\alpha\_{s}\right|^{2}ds<\infty, ‚Ąô\mathbb{P}-a.s.;

The set of all admissible investment strategies is denoted as ūĚíú{\mathcal{A}} and is naturally defined by

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | ūĚíú={őĪ‚ąąLūĚĒĹ2,l‚Äčo‚Äčc([0,T],‚ĄĚd)¬†such that ([3.30](#S3.E30 "In 3.1 Optimal strategy for the power utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) has a solution satisfying¬†([3.32](#S3.E32 "In 3.1 Optimal strategy for the power utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")).}\mathcal{A}=\left\{\alpha\in{L^{2,loc}\_{\mathbb{F}}([0,T],\mathbb{R}^{d})}\mbox{ such that \eqref{Eq:wealth} has a solution satisfying }\penalty 10000\ \eqref{eq:estimateXPower}.\right\} |  |

We want to solve the Merton power utility optimization problem, i.e. our aim is to find the value function ūĚíĪ‚Äč(x0,V0)\mathcal{V}(x\_{0},V\_{0}) for the CRRA utility function such that

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | ūĚíĪ‚Äč(x0,V0)=supőĪ‚Äč(‚čÖ)‚ąąūĚíúūĚĒľx0,V0‚Äč[1ő≥‚Äč(XTőĪ)ő≥];0<ő≥<1,\mathcal{V}(x\_{0},V\_{0})=\sup\_{\alpha(\cdot)\in{\mathcal{A}}}\mathbb{E}\_{x\_{0},V\_{0}}[\frac{1}{\gamma}(X\_{T}^{\alpha})^{\gamma}];\quad 0<\gamma<1, |  | (3.33) |

where ūĚĒľx0,V0\mathbb{E}\_{x\_{0},V\_{0}} is the conditional expectation given x0x\_{0} and V0V\_{0}. The parameter ő≥\gamma represents the relative
risk aversion of the investor. Smaller ő≥\gamma correspond to higher risk aversion.
A strategy őĪ‚ąó\alpha^{\*} for which the supremum is attained is called an optimal strategy.

#### 3.1.1 The degenerate correlation case

We assume that the correlation in ([2.15](#S2.E15 "In 2.2 Formulation of the stochastic Market model ‚Ä£ 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) is of the form (ŌĀ,‚Ä¶,ŌĀ)(\rho,\dots,\rho) for ŌĀ‚ąą[‚ąí1,1]\rho\in[-1,1]. To construct the family of processes {JtőĪ}t‚ąą[0,T]\{J^{\alpha}\_{t}\}\_{t\in[0,T]}, őĪ‚ąąūĚíú\alpha\in{\mathcal{A}}, satisfying conditions (1)(1)- (2)(2)- (3)(3) in Definition [3.2](#S3.ThmTheorem2 "Definition 3.2 (Martingale optimality principle). ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models"), we introduce the new probability measure ‚Ąô~\tilde{\mathbb{P}} defined via the Radon-Nikodym density at ‚ĄĪT\mathcal{F}\_{T} from

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | d‚Äč‚Ąô~d‚Äč‚Ąô|‚ĄĪt=‚Ąį‚Äč(ő≥1‚ąíő≥‚Äč‚ąę0t‚ąĎi=1dőłi‚ÄčVsi‚Äčd‚ÄčBsi)=exp‚Ā°(ő≥1‚ąíő≥‚Äč‚ąę0tőĽs‚ä§‚ÄčūĚĎĎBs‚ąíő≥22‚Äč(1‚ąíő≥)2‚Äč‚ąę0t|őĽs|2‚ÄčūĚĎĎs)\frac{d\tilde{\mathbb{P}}}{d\mathbb{P}}|\_{\mathcal{F}\_{t}}=\mathcal{E}\Big(\frac{\gamma}{1-\gamma}\int\_{0}^{t}\sum\_{i=1}^{d}\theta\_{i}\sqrt{V^{i}\_{s}}dB^{i}\_{s}\Big)=\operatorname{exp}\Big(\frac{\gamma}{1-\gamma}\int\_{0}^{t}\lambda\_{s}^{\top}dB\_{s}-\frac{\gamma^{2}}{2(1-\gamma)^{2}}\int\_{0}^{t}\left|\lambda\_{s}\right|^{2}ds\Big) |  |

where the stochastic exponential is a true martingale by Lemma [5.1](#S5.ThmTheorem1 "Lemma 5.1 (Martingale property of stochastic exponentials). ‚Ä£ 5 Proofs of the main results ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")
together with the new standard brownian motion under ‚Ąô~\tilde{\mathbb{P}}, B~t=Bt‚ąíő≥1‚ąíő≥‚Äč‚ąę0tőĽs‚ÄčūĚĎĎs\widetilde{B}\_{t}=B\_{t}-\frac{\gamma}{1-\gamma}\int\_{0}^{t}\lambda\_{s}ds.
Define the new process W~\widetilde{W} by

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | W~t=ő£‚ÄčB~t+I‚ąíő£‚ä§‚Äčő£‚ÄčBt‚üā=Wt‚ąíő≥1‚ąíő≥‚Äč‚ąę0tő£‚ÄčőĽs‚ÄčūĚĎĎs,\widetilde{W}\_{t}=\Sigma\widetilde{B}\_{t}+\sqrt{I-\Sigma^{\top}\Sigma}B^{\perp}\_{t}=W\_{t}-\frac{\gamma}{1-\gamma}\int\_{0}^{t}\Sigma\lambda\_{s}ds, |  |

Notice that, by the Girsanov theorem, B~\widetilde{B} and W~\widetilde{W} are standard Wiener processes under the measure ‚Ąô~\tilde{\mathbb{P}}.
As in the one dimensional case, the Ansatz (őī\delta is called the distorsion coefficient)

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | JtőĪ=(XtőĪ)ő≥ő≥(ūĚĒľ‚Ąô~[exp(‚ąętTő≥őī(rs+|őĽs|22‚Äč(1‚ąíő≥))ds)|‚ĄĪt])őī=:(XtőĪ)ő≥ő≥őďtwhereőī:=1‚ąíő≥1‚ąíő≥+ő≥‚ÄčŌĀ2.J\_{t}^{\alpha}=\frac{(X\_{t}^{\alpha})^{\gamma}}{\gamma}\Big(\mathbb{E}^{\tilde{\mathbb{P}}}\Big[\operatorname{exp}\Big(\int\_{t}^{T}\frac{\gamma}{\delta}\Big(r\_{s}+\frac{\left|\lambda\_{s}\right|^{2}}{2(1-\gamma)}\Big)ds\Big)|\mathcal{F}\_{t}\Big]\Big)^{\delta}=:\frac{(X\_{t}^{\alpha})^{\gamma}}{\gamma}\Gamma\_{t}\quad\text{where}\quad\delta:=\frac{1-\gamma}{1-\gamma+\gamma\rho^{2}}. |  |

is inspired by the martingale distortion transformation which was first introduced in the seminal paper Zariphopoulou ([2001](#bib.bib34)) and later transferred to a non-Markovian setting in Tehranchi ([2004](#bib.bib30)); Fouque and Hu ([2019](#bib.bib12)).
Here we use the short notation JtőĪJ\_{t}^{\alpha} for Jt‚Äč(XtőĪ,Vt)J\_{t}(X\_{t}^{\alpha},V\_{t}).

The main properties of őďt\Gamma\_{t} are summarized in Proposition [3.4](#S3.ThmTheorem4 "Proposition 3.4. ‚Ä£ 3.1.1 The degenerate correlation case ‚Ä£ 3.1 Optimal strategy for the power utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models") below where g~t‚Äč(s)\tilde{g}\_{t}(s) denotes the conditional ‚Ąô~\tilde{\mathbb{P}}-expected ajusted variance process.

###### Proposition 3.4.

Assume that there exists a solution Ōą‚ąąC‚Äč([0,T],‚ĄĚd)\psi\in C([0,T],\mathbb{R}^{d}) to the inhomogeneous Riccati-Volterra equation ([3.34](#S3.E34 "In Proposition 3.4. ‚Ä£ 3.1.1 The degenerate correlation case ‚Ä£ 3.1 Optimal strategy for the power utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models"))-([3.35](#S3.E35 "In Proposition 3.4. ‚Ä£ 3.1.1 The degenerate correlation case ‚Ä£ 3.1 Optimal strategy for the power utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) below:

|  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | Ōąi‚Äč(t)\displaystyle\psi^{i}(t) | =‚ąę0tKi‚Äč(t‚ąís)‚Äč(ő≥‚Äčőłi22‚Äčőī‚Äč(1‚ąíő≥)+Fi‚Äč(T‚ąís,Ōą‚Äč(s)))‚ÄčūĚĎĎs,\displaystyle=\int\_{0}^{t}K\_{i}(t-s)\big(\frac{\gamma\theta\_{i}^{2}}{2\delta(1-\gamma)}+F\_{i}(T-s,\psi(s))\big)ds, |  | (3.34) |
|  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | Fi‚Äč(s,Ōą)\displaystyle F\_{i}(s,\psi) | =ő≥1‚ąíő≥‚ÄčŌĀ‚Äčőłi‚ÄčőĹi‚ÄčŌāi‚Äč(s)‚ÄčŌąi+(D‚ä§‚ÄčŌą)i+őĹi22‚Äč(Ōāi‚Äč(s)‚ÄčŌąi)2,i=1,‚Ä¶,d,\displaystyle=\frac{\gamma}{1-\gamma}\rho\theta\_{i}\nu\_{i}\varsigma^{i}(s)\psi^{i}+(D^{\top}\psi)\_{i}+\frac{\nu\_{i}^{2}}{2}(\varsigma^{i}(s)\psi^{i})^{2},\quad i=1,\ldots,d, |  | (3.35) |

Then,

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | őďt=exp‚Ā°(ő≥‚Äč‚ąętTr‚Äč(s)‚ÄčūĚĎĎs+‚ąĎi=1d‚ąętT(ő≥‚Äčőłi22‚Äč(1‚ąíő≥)+őī‚ÄčFi‚Äč(s,Ōą‚Äč(T‚ąís)))‚Äčg~ti‚Äč(s)‚ÄčūĚĎĎs).\Gamma\_{t}=\exp\Big(\gamma\int\_{t}^{T}r(s)ds+\sum\_{i=1}^{d}\int\_{t}^{T}\big(\frac{\gamma\theta\_{i}^{2}}{2(1-\gamma)}+\delta F\_{i}(s,\psi(T-s))\big)\tilde{g}^{i}\_{t}(s)ds\Big). |  | (3.36) |

where g~=(g~1,‚Ä¶,g~d)‚ä§\tilde{g}=(\tilde{g}^{1},\ldots,\tilde{g}^{d})^{\top} is the ‚ĄĚd\mathbb{R}^{d}-valued process (g~t‚Äč(s))t‚Č§s(\tilde{g}\_{t}(s))\_{t\leq s} denoting the adjusted conditional ‚Ąô~\tilde{\mathbb{P}}-expected variance.
Moreover (őď,őõ)‚ąąūĚēäūĚĒĹp‚Äč([0,T],‚ĄĚ+‚ąó)√óLūĚĒĹ2‚Äč([0,T],‚ĄĚd)\left(\Gamma,\Lambda\right)\in\mathbb{S}^{p}\_{\mathbb{F}}([0,T],\mathbb{R}\_{+}^{\*})\times L^{2}\_{\mathbb{F}}([0,T],\mathbb{R}^{d}) for some sufficiently large p>1‚ąß1‚ąíő≥ő≥p>1\wedge\frac{1-\gamma}{\gamma} and satisfy the following Riccati BSDE

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | d‚Äčőďtőďt\displaystyle\frac{d\Gamma\_{t}}{\Gamma\_{t}} | =(‚ąíő≥‚Äčr‚Äč(t)‚ąíő≥2‚Äč(1‚ąíő≥)‚Äč‚ąĎi=1d(őłi2+őī2‚ÄčŌĀ2‚ÄčőĹi2‚Äč(Ōāi‚Äč(t)‚ÄčŌąi‚Äč(T‚ąít))2)‚ÄčVti)‚Äčd‚Äčt+őī‚Äč‚ąĎi=1dŌąi‚Äč(T‚ąít)‚ÄčőĹi‚ÄčŌāi‚Äč(t)‚ÄčVti‚Äčd‚ÄčW~ti\displaystyle=\Big(-\gamma r(t)-\frac{\gamma}{2(1-\gamma)}\sum\_{i=1}^{d}\Big(\theta\_{i}^{2}+\delta^{2}\rho^{2}\nu\_{i}^{2}(\varsigma^{i}(t)\psi^{i}(T-t))^{2}\Big)V^{i}\_{t}\Big)dt+\;\delta\sum\_{i=1}^{d}\psi^{i}(T-t)\nu\_{i}\varsigma^{i}(t)\sqrt{V^{i}\_{t}}d\widetilde{W}^{i}\_{t} |  |
|  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  |  | =(‚ąíő≥‚Äčr‚Äč(t)‚ąíő≥2‚Äč(1‚ąíő≥)‚Äč|őĽt|2‚ąíő≥2‚Äč(1‚ąíő≥)‚Äčőī2‚Äč|ő£‚Äčőõt|2)‚Äčd‚Äčt+őī‚Äčőõt‚ä§‚Äčd‚ÄčW~t,őďT=1.\displaystyle=\big(-\gamma r(t)-\frac{\gamma}{2(1-\gamma)}\left|\lambda\_{t}\right|^{2}-\frac{\gamma}{2(1-\gamma)}\delta^{2}\left|\Sigma\Lambda\_{t}\right|^{2}\big)dt+\delta\Lambda\_{t}^{\top}d\widetilde{W}\_{t},\quad\Gamma\_{T}=1. |  | (3.37) |

Note that Equation ([5.1](#S5.Ex52 "5.1 Proofs of Proposition 3.4 and Theorems 3.5 and 3.7 ‚Ä£ 5 Proofs of the main results ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) is known in the litterature as a Ricatti backward stochastic differential equation (see e.g. (Abi Jaber et al., [2021](#bib.bib2), Theorem 3.1) or (Chiu and Wong, [2014](#bib.bib8), heorem 3.1), upon setting őõ~t=őďt‚Äčőõt\tilde{\Lambda}\_{t}=\Gamma\_{t}\Lambda\_{t} ).

Existence and uniqueness of the solution to ([3.34](#S3.E34 "In Proposition 3.4. ‚Ä£ 3.1.1 The degenerate correlation case ‚Ä£ 3.1 Optimal strategy for the power utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models"))-([3.35](#S3.E35 "In Proposition 3.4. ‚Ä£ 3.1.1 The degenerate correlation case ‚Ä£ 3.1 Optimal strategy for the power utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) are established in (Gnabeyeu, [2026](#bib.bib14), Theorem A.1) based on the results of Gnabeyeu et al. ([b](#bib.bib17)) (see also the Remark on Proposition [3.6](#S3.ThmTheorem6 "Proposition 3.6. ‚Ä£ 3.1.2 The general correlation case: A verification argument ‚Ä£ 3.1 Optimal strategy for the power utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")).

By considering őďt\Gamma\_{t}, we overcome the non-Markovian and non-semimartingale difficulty in the variance process ([2.2](#S2.E2 "In 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")).
Now we are ready to give the Ansatz for JtőĪJ^{\alpha}\_{t}. Consider

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | JtőĪ=Xtő≥ő≥‚Äčőďt.J^{\alpha}\_{t}=\frac{X^{\gamma}\_{t}}{\gamma}\Gamma\_{t}. |  | (3.38) |

The main result we provide for this case is the following:

###### Theorem 3.5.

Let Ōą\psi be the unique, continuous non-continuable solution of the inhomogeneous Ricatti-Volterra equation ([3.34](#S3.E34 "In Proposition 3.4. ‚Ä£ 3.1.1 The degenerate correlation case ‚Ä£ 3.1 Optimal strategy for the power utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models"))- ([3.35](#S3.E35 "In Proposition 3.4. ‚Ä£ 3.1.1 The degenerate correlation case ‚Ä£ 3.1 Optimal strategy for the power utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models"))
on the interval [0,Tmax)[0,T\_{\text{max}}) so that Assumption [3.1](#S3.Thmassumption1 "Assumption 3.1. ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models") is in force. Then JtőĪ=(XtőĪ)ő≥ő≥‚ÄčőďtJ^{\alpha}\_{t}=\frac{(X\_{t}^{\alpha})^{\gamma}}{\gamma}\Gamma\_{t} satisfies the martingale optimality principle for t‚ąą[0,T]t\in[0,T], T<TmaxT<T\_{\text{max}}, and the optimal portfolio strategy őĪ‚ąó\alpha^{\*} is given by

|  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | őĪt‚ąó\displaystyle\alpha^{\*}\_{t} | =11‚ąíő≥‚Äč(őĽt+őī‚Äčő£‚Äčőõt)=11‚ąíő≥‚Äčdiag‚Ā°(Vt)‚Äč(őł+őī‚Äčő£‚ÄčőĹ‚ÄčŌā‚Äč(t)‚ÄčŌą‚Äč(T‚ąít)),0‚Č§t‚Č§T\displaystyle=\frac{1}{1-\gamma}\left(\lambda\_{t}+\delta\Sigma\Lambda\_{t}\right)=\frac{1}{1-\gamma}\sqrt{\operatorname{diag}(V\_{t})}\left(\theta+\delta\Sigma\nu\varsigma(t)\psi(T-t)\right),\quad 0\leq t\leq T |  | (3.39) |
|  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  |  | =(11‚ąíő≥‚Äč(őłi+őī‚ÄčŌĀ‚ÄčőĹi‚ÄčŌāi‚Äč(t)‚ÄčŌąi‚Äč(T‚ąít))‚ÄčVti)1‚Č§i‚Č§d,0‚Č§t‚Č§T.\displaystyle=\;\Big(\frac{1}{1-\gamma}\big(\theta\_{i}+\delta\rho\nu\_{i}\varsigma^{i}(t)\psi^{i}(T-t)\big)\sqrt{V\_{t}^{i}}\Big)\_{1\leq i\leq d},\quad 0\leq t\leq T. |  | (3.40) |

Moreover, XőĪ‚ąóX^{\alpha^{\*}} satisfies ([3.32](#S3.E32 "In 3.1 Optimal strategy for the power utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models"))
and őĪ‚ąó\alpha^{\*} is admissible.

#### 3.1.2 The general correlation case: A verification argument

The martingale distortion approach, used by Han and Wong ([2020](#bib.bib19)) in the one dimensional case
can only be applied to the multivariate setting if the correlation structure is highly degenerate, i.e. ŌĀ1=‚Ä¶=ŌĀd.\rho\_{1}=\ldots=\rho\_{d}. (see also Fouque and Hu ([2019](#bib.bib12)); Aichinger and Desmettre ([2021](#bib.bib3))).
For the case where the correlation in ([2.15](#S2.E15 "In 2.2 Formulation of the stochastic Market model ‚Ä£ 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) is given by an arbitrary vector (ŌĀ1,‚Ä¶,ŌĀd)‚ąą[‚ąí1,1]d(\rho\_{1},\dots,\rho\_{d})\in[-1,1]^{d}, the martingale distortion arguments from the previous section do not work anymore. However, we remark that when ŌĀ1=‚Ä¶=ŌĀd=ŌĀ\rho\_{1}=\ldots=\rho\_{d}=\rho, if Ōą\psi is the unique global solution of the Riccati‚ÄďVolterra equation ([3.34](#S3.E34 "In Proposition 3.4. ‚Ä£ 3.1.1 The degenerate correlation case ‚Ä£ 3.1 Optimal strategy for the power utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models"))‚Äď ([3.35](#S3.E35 "In Proposition 3.4. ‚Ä£ 3.1.1 The degenerate correlation case ‚Ä£ 3.1 Optimal strategy for the power utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")), then setting Ōą~=őī‚ÄčŌą\tilde{\psi}=\delta\,\psi and őł=diag‚Ā°(őł1,‚Ä¶,őłd)\theta=\operatorname{diag}{(\theta\_{1},\dots,\theta\_{d})}, we have using őī=1‚ąíő≥1‚ąíő≥+ő≥‚ÄčŌĀ2\delta=\frac{1-\gamma}{1-\gamma+\gamma\rho^{2}}

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | őī‚ÄčF‚Äč(s,Ōą)\displaystyle\delta F(s,\psi) | =ő≥1‚ąíő≥‚ÄčőĹ‚ÄčŌā‚Äč(s)‚Äčő£‚Äčőł‚Äč(őī‚ÄčŌą)+D‚ä§‚Äč(őī‚ÄčŌą)+12‚Äčőī‚Äč(őĹ‚ÄčŌā‚Äč(s)‚Äč(őī‚ÄčŌą))2\displaystyle=\frac{\gamma}{1-\gamma}\nu\varsigma(s)\Sigma\theta(\delta\psi)+D^{\top}(\delta\psi)+\frac{1}{2\delta}\Big(\nu\varsigma(s)(\delta\psi)\Big)^{2} |  |
|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  |  | =ő≥1‚ąíő≥‚ÄčőĹ‚ÄčŌā‚Äč(s)‚Äčő£‚Äčőł‚Äč(őī‚ÄčŌą)+D‚ä§‚Äč(őī‚ÄčŌą)+12‚Äč[(őĹ‚ÄčŌā‚Äč(s)‚Äč(őī‚ÄčŌą))2+ő≥1‚ąíő≥‚Äč(őĹ‚ÄčŌā‚Äč(s)‚Äčő£‚Äč(őī‚ÄčŌą))2]=F~‚Äč(s,Ōą~)\displaystyle=\frac{\gamma}{1-\gamma}\nu\varsigma(s)\Sigma\theta(\delta\psi)+D^{\top}(\delta\psi)+\frac{1}{2}\left[\Big(\nu\varsigma(s)(\delta\psi)\Big)^{2}+\frac{\gamma}{1-\gamma}\Big(\nu\varsigma(s)\Sigma(\delta\psi)\Big)^{2}\right]=\tilde{F}(s,\tilde{\psi}) |  |

where F~‚Äč(s,Ōą~):=ő≥1‚ąíő≥‚ÄčőĹ‚ÄčŌā‚Äč(s)‚Äčő£‚Äčőł‚ÄčŌą~+D‚ä§‚ÄčŌą~+12‚Äč[(őĹ‚ÄčŌā‚Äč(s)‚ÄčŌą~)2+ő≥1‚ąíő≥‚Äč(őĹ‚ÄčŌā‚Äč(s)‚Äčő£‚ÄčŌą~)2]\tilde{F}(s,\tilde{\psi}):=\frac{\gamma}{1-\gamma}\nu\varsigma(s)\Sigma\theta\tilde{\psi}+D^{\top}\tilde{\psi}+\frac{1}{2}\left[(\nu\varsigma(s)\tilde{\psi})^{2}+\frac{\gamma}{1-\gamma}(\nu\varsigma(s)\Sigma\tilde{\psi})^{2}\right] so that Ōą~‚ąąC‚Äč([0,T],‚ĄĚd)\tilde{\psi}\in C([0,T],\mathbb{R}^{d}) is the unique global solution of the inhomogeneous Riccati‚ÄďVolterra equation

|  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | Ōą~i‚Äč(t)\displaystyle\tilde{\psi}^{i}(t) | =‚ąę0tKi‚Äč(t‚ąís)‚Äč(ő≥‚Äčőłi22‚Äč(1‚ąíő≥)+F~i‚Äč(T‚ąís,Ōą~‚Äč(s)))‚ÄčūĚĎĎs,\displaystyle=\int\_{0}^{t}K\_{i}(t-s)\big(\frac{\gamma\theta\_{i}^{2}}{2(1-\gamma)}+\tilde{F}\_{i}(T-s,\tilde{\psi}(s))\big)ds, |  | (3.41) |
|  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | F~i‚Äč(s,Ōą~)\displaystyle\tilde{F}\_{i}(s,\tilde{\psi}) | =ő≥1‚ąíő≥‚Äčőłi‚ÄčŌĀi‚ÄčőĹi‚ÄčŌāi‚Äč(s)‚ÄčŌą~i+(D‚ä§‚ÄčŌą~)i+őĹi22‚Äč[(Ōāi‚Äč(s)‚ÄčŌą~i)2+ő≥1‚ąíő≥‚ÄčŌĀi2‚Äč(Ōāi‚Äč(s)‚ÄčŌą~i)2],i=1,‚Ä¶,d,\displaystyle=\frac{\gamma}{1-\gamma}\theta\_{i}\rho\_{i}\nu\_{i}\varsigma^{i}(s)\tilde{\psi}^{i}+(D^{\top}\tilde{\psi})\_{i}+\frac{\nu\_{i}^{2}}{2}\left[(\varsigma^{i}(s)\tilde{\psi}^{i})^{2}+\frac{\gamma}{1-\gamma}\rho\_{i}^{2}(\varsigma^{i}(s)\tilde{\psi}^{i})^{2}\right],\quad i=1,\ldots,d, |  | (3.42) |

Consequently, to avoid restrictions on the correlation structure linked to the martingale distortion transformation, we use a verification arguments in the spirit of B√§uerle and Li ([2013](#bib.bib6)) to solve the optimization problem, thus extending the results obtained in the preveous section to the more general correlation structure.

###### Proposition 3.6.

Assume that there exists a solution Ōą‚ąąC‚Äč([0,T],‚ĄĚd)\psi\in C([0,T],\mathbb{R}^{d}) to the inhomogeneous Riccati-Volterra equation:

|  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | Ōąi‚Äč(t)\displaystyle\qquad\;\psi^{i}(t) | =‚ąę0tKi‚Äč(t‚ąís)‚Äč(ő≥‚Äčőłi22‚Äč(1‚ąíő≥)+Fi‚Äč(T‚ąís,Ōą‚Äč(s)))‚ÄčūĚĎĎs,\displaystyle=\int\_{0}^{t}K\_{i}(t-s)\big(\frac{\gamma\theta\_{i}^{2}}{2(1-\gamma)}+F\_{i}(T-s,\psi(s))\big)ds, |  | (3.43) |
|  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | Fi‚Äč(s,Ōą)\displaystyle F\_{i}(s,\psi) | =ő≥1‚ąíő≥‚Äčőłi‚ÄčŌĀi‚ÄčőĹi‚ÄčŌāi‚Äč(s)‚ÄčŌąi+(D‚ä§‚ÄčŌą)i+őĹi22‚Äč[(Ōāi‚Äč(s)‚ÄčŌąi)2+ő≥1‚ąíő≥‚ÄčŌĀi2‚Äč(Ōāi‚Äč(s)‚ÄčŌąi)2],i=1,‚Ä¶,d.\displaystyle=\frac{\gamma}{1-\gamma}\theta\_{i}\rho\_{i}\nu\_{i}\varsigma^{i}(s)\psi^{i}+(D^{\top}\psi)\_{i}+\frac{\nu\_{i}^{2}}{2}\left[(\varsigma^{i}(s)\psi^{i})^{2}+\frac{\gamma}{1-\gamma}\rho\_{i}^{2}(\varsigma^{i}(s)\psi^{i})^{2}\right],\;i=1,\ldots,d. |  | (3.44) |

Let (őď,őõ)\left(\Gamma,\Lambda\right) be defined as

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |

Proof:  The proof that (őď,őõ)\left(\Gamma,\Lambda\right) satisfy ([3.46](#S3.E46 "In Proposition 3.6. ‚Ä£ 3.1.2 The general correlation case: A verification argument ‚Ä£ 3.1 Optimal strategy for the power utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) is a straightforward adaptation of the arguments from the proof of Proposition [3.4](#S3.ThmTheorem4 "Proposition 3.4. ‚Ä£ 3.1.1 The degenerate correlation case ‚Ä£ 3.1 Optimal strategy for the power utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models").

An application of It√ī‚Äôs formula to the process

|  |  |  |
