|  | M¬Įt:=őďt‚Äčexp‚Ā°(‚ąę0t(ő≥‚Äčr‚Äč(s)+ő≥2‚Äč(1‚ąíő≥)‚Äč|őĽs+ő£‚Äčőõs|2)‚ÄčūĚĎĎs),t‚Č§T,\bar{M}\_{t}:=\Gamma\_{t}\exp\Big(\int\_{0}^{t}\big(\gamma r(s)+\frac{\gamma}{2(1-\gamma)}\left|\lambda\_{s}+\Sigma\Lambda\_{s}\right|^{2}\big)ds\Big),\;t\leq T, |  |

combined with the dynamics ([3.46](#S3.E46 "In Proposition 3.6. ‚Ä£ 3.1.2 The general correlation case: A verification argument ‚Ä£ 3.1 Optimal strategy for the power utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) shows that d‚ÄčM¬Įt=M¬Įt‚Äčőõt‚ä§‚Äčd‚ÄčWtd\bar{M}\_{t}=\bar{M}\_{t}\Lambda\_{t}^{\top}dW\_{t}, so that M¬Į\bar{M} is a local martingale of the form M¬Įt=‚Ąį‚Äč(‚ąę0tőõs‚ä§‚ÄčūĚĎĎWs)=‚Ąį‚Äč(‚ąę0t‚ąĎi=1dőĹi‚ÄčŌāi‚Äč(s)‚ÄčŌąi‚Äč(T‚ąís)‚ÄčVsi‚Äčd‚ÄčWsi).\bar{M}\_{t}=\;\mathcal{E}\Big(\int\_{0}^{t}\Lambda\_{s}^{\top}dW\_{s}\Big)=\;\mathcal{E}\Big(\int\_{0}^{t}\sum\_{i=1}^{d}\nu\_{i}\varsigma^{i}(s)\psi^{i}(T-s)\sqrt{V^{i}\_{s}}dW^{i}\_{s}\Big).
Since Ōą\psi is continuous, it is bounded; likewise, Ōā\varsigma is bounded. Therefore a straightforward application of Lemma [5.1](#S5.ThmTheorem1 "Lemma 5.1 (Martingale property of stochastic exponentials). ‚Ä£ 5 Proofs of the main results ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models") with g2=0g\_{2}=0 and g1,i‚Äč(s)=őĹi‚ÄčŌāi‚Äč(s)‚ÄčŌąi‚Äč(T‚ąís)‚ąąL‚ąě‚Äč([0,T],‚ĄĚ)g\_{1,i}(s)=\nu\_{i}\varsigma^{i}(s)\psi^{i}(T-s)\in L^{\infty}([0,T],\mathbb{R}), recall ([2.17](#S2.E17 "In Theorem 2.7. ‚Ä£ 2.2 Formulation of the stochastic Market model ‚Ä£ 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")), yields that the stochastic exponential M¬Į\bar{M} is a true ‚Ąô\mathbb{P}- martingale. Now, as őďT=1\Gamma\_{T}=1, writing ūĚĒľ‚Äč[M¬ĮT|‚ĄĪt]=M¬Įt\mathbb{E}[\bar{M}\_{T}|\mathcal{F}\_{t}]=\bar{M}\_{t}, we obtain

|  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | őďt\displaystyle\Gamma\_{t} | =ūĚĒľ‚Äč[exp‚Ā°(‚ąętT(ő≥‚Äčr‚Äč(s)+ő≥2‚Äč(1‚ąíő≥)‚Äč|őĽs+ő£‚Äčőõs|2)‚ÄčūĚĎĎs)‚ą£‚ĄĪt],t‚Č§T\displaystyle=\mathbb{E}\Big[\exp\Big(\int\_{t}^{T}\big(\gamma r(s)+\frac{\gamma}{2(1-\gamma)}\left|\lambda\_{s}+\Sigma\Lambda\_{s}\right|^{2}\big)ds\Big)\mid\mathcal{F}\_{t}\Big],\quad t\leq T |  | (3.47) |

|  |  | ‚Č§exp‚Ā°(‚ąę0Tő≥‚Äčr‚Äč(s)‚ÄčūĚĎĎs)‚ÄčMt,with‚ÄčMt:=ūĚĒľ‚Äč[exp‚Ā°(ő≥2‚Äč(1‚ąíő≥)‚Äč‚ąę0T|őĽs+ő£‚Äčőõs|2‚ÄčūĚĎĎs)‚ą£‚ĄĪt],t‚Č§T\displaystyle\leq\exp\Big(\int\_{0}^{T}\gamma r(s)ds\Big)M\_{t},\;\text{with}\;M\_{t}:=\mathbb{E}\Big[\exp\Big(\frac{\gamma}{2(1-\gamma)}\int\_{0}^{T}\left|\lambda\_{s}+\Sigma\Lambda\_{s}\right|^{2}ds\Big)\mid\mathcal{F}\_{t}\Big],\quad t\leq T |  |

We then have in view of ([3.47](#S3.E47 "In 3.1.2 The general correlation case: A verification argument ‚Ä£ 3.1 Optimal strategy for the power utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) that there exists some positive constant m>0m>0 such that őďt‚Č•m>0\Gamma\_{t}\geq m>0 for every t‚ąą[0,T]t\in[0,T].
Using the elementary inequality (a+b)p‚Č§2(p‚ąí1)+‚Äč(ap+bp)(a+b)^{p}\leq 2^{(p-1)^{+}}\big(a^{p}+b^{p}\big) for a,b>0a,b>0, one gets

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | |őĽs+ő£‚Äčőõs|2‚Č§2‚Äč(|őĽs|2+|ő£‚Äčőõs|2)‚Č§2‚Äč(1+|ő£|2)‚Äč(|őĽs|2+|őõs|2)‚Č§2‚Äčő≤‚Äč(1+|ő£|2)‚Äč(|őĽs|2+|őõs|2).|\lambda\_{s}+\Sigma\Lambda\_{s}|^{2}\leq 2(|\lambda\_{s}|^{2}+|\Sigma\Lambda\_{s}|^{2})\leq 2(1+|\Sigma|^{2})(|\lambda\_{s}|^{2}+|\Lambda\_{s}|^{2})\leq 2\beta(1+|\Sigma|^{2})(|\lambda\_{s}|^{2}+|\Lambda\_{s}|^{2}). |  |

where ő≤>1\beta>1 is choosen such that ő≤‚Äčő≥(1‚ąíő≥)>1\frac{\beta\gamma}{(1-\gamma)}>1. Consequently, by simple calculation:

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | ūĚĒľ‚Äč[exp‚Ā°(ő≥2‚Äč(1‚ąíő≥)‚Äč‚ąę0T|őĽs+ő£‚Äčőõs|2‚ÄčūĚĎĎs)]\displaystyle\mathbb{E}\Big[\exp\Big(\frac{\gamma}{2(1-\gamma)}\int\_{0}^{T}\left|\lambda\_{s}+\Sigma\Lambda\_{s}\right|^{2}ds\Big)\Big] | ‚Č§ūĚĒľ‚Äč[exp‚Ā°(ő≤‚Äčő≥(1‚ąíő≥)‚Äč(1+|ő£|2)‚Äč‚ąę0T(|őĽs|2+|őõs|2)‚ÄčūĚĎĎs)]<‚ąě\displaystyle\leq\mathbb{E}\Big[\exp\Big(\frac{\beta\gamma}{(1-\gamma)}(1+|\Sigma|^{2})\int\_{0}^{T}\big(|\lambda\_{s}|^{2}+|\Lambda\_{s}|^{2}\big)ds\Big)\Big]<\infty |  |

thanks to the Novikov-type condition ([3.27](#S3.E27 "In 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) with constant a‚Äč(ő≤‚Äčő≥(1‚ąíő≥))=ő≤‚Äčő≥(1‚ąíő≥)‚Äč(1+|ő£|2)a(\frac{\beta\gamma}{(1-\gamma)})=\frac{\beta\gamma}{(1-\gamma)}(1+|\Sigma|^{2}). Therefore, MtM\_{t} is a martingale under ‚Ąô\mathbb{P}.
Let p>1‚ąß1‚ąíő≥ő≥p>1\wedge\frac{1-\gamma}{\gamma}.
By virtue of Doob‚Äôs maximal inequality, in the second line,

As for őõ\Lambda, it is clear that it belongs to LūĚĒĹ2‚Äč([0,T],‚ĄĚd)L^{2}\_{\mathbb{F}}([0,T],\mathbb{R}^{d}) since Ōā\varsigma and Ōą\psi are bounded, Ōą\psi is continuous thus bounded and ūĚĒľ‚Äč[‚ąę0T‚ąĎi=1dVsi‚Äčd‚Äčs]<‚ąě\mathbb{E}\Big[\int\_{0}^{T}\sum\_{i=1}^{d}V^{i}\_{s}ds\Big]<\infty by ([2.17](#S2.E17 "In Theorem 2.7. ‚Ä£ 2.2 Formulation of the stochastic Market model ‚Ä£ 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")). First of all, we point out that for each of the inhomogeneous Riccati-Volterra equations ([3.43](#S3.E43 "In Proposition 3.6. ‚Ä£ 3.1.2 The general correlation case: A verification argument ‚Ä£ 3.1 Optimal strategy for the power utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models"))- ([3.44](#S3.E44 "In Proposition 3.6. ‚Ä£ 3.1.2 The general correlation case: A verification argument ‚Ä£ 3.1 Optimal strategy for the power utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) and ([3.34](#S3.E34 "In Proposition 3.4. ‚Ä£ 3.1.1 The degenerate correlation case ‚Ä£ 3.1 Optimal strategy for the power utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models"))- ([3.35](#S3.E35 "In Proposition 3.4. ‚Ä£ 3.1.1 The degenerate correlation case ‚Ä£ 3.1 Optimal strategy for the power utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")), there exists a unique non-continuable continuous solution (Ōą,Tmax)(\psi,T\_{\operatorname{max}}) under Assumption [2.1](#S2.Thmassumption1 "Assumption 2.1 (On Volterra Equations with convolutive kernels). ‚Ä£ 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models") by (Gnabeyeu, [2026](#bib.bib14), Theorem A.1) as stated in the following Remark.

Remark: Fix T>0T>0
and assume that KK satisfies Assumption [2.1](#S2.Thmassumption1 "Assumption 2.1 (On Volterra Equations with convolutive kernels). ‚Ä£ 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models"). As the matrix DD in the drift of the volatility process is a diagonal matrix, i.e. D=‚ąídiag‚Ā°(őĽ1,‚Ä¶,őĽd)D=-\operatorname{diag}{(\lambda\_{1},\dots,\lambda\_{d})}, for i=1,‚Ä¶,d,i=1,\ldots,d, Ōąi\psi^{i} satisfies the Volterra equation

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | Ōá‚Äč(t)=‚ąę0tKi‚Äč(t‚ąís)‚Äč(ő≥‚Äčőłi22‚Äč(1‚ąíő≥)‚ąí(őĽi‚ąíő≥1‚ąíő≥‚Äčőłi‚ÄčŌĀi‚ÄčőĹi‚ÄčŌāi‚Äč(T‚ąís))‚ÄčŌá‚Äč(s)+őĹi22‚Äč1‚ąíő≥+ő≥‚ÄčŌĀi21‚ąíő≥‚ÄčŌāi‚Äč(T‚ąís)2‚ÄčŌá‚Äč(s)2)‚ÄčūĚĎĎs,t‚Č§T.\chi(t)=\int\_{0}^{t}K\_{i}(t-s)\Big(\frac{\gamma\theta\_{i}^{2}}{2(1-\gamma)}-\big(\lambda\_{i}-\frac{\gamma}{1-\gamma}\theta\_{i}\rho\_{i}\nu\_{i}\varsigma^{i}(T-s)\big)\chi(s)+\frac{\nu\_{i}^{2}}{2}\frac{1-\gamma+\gamma\rho\_{i}^{2}}{1-\gamma}\varsigma^{i}(T-s)^{2}\chi(s)^{2}\Big)ds,\;t\leq T. |  | (3.48) |

(Gnabeyeu, [2026](#bib.bib14), Theorem A.1) guarantees that there exists a unique non-continuable continuous solution (Ōą,Tmax)(\psi,T\_{\max}) to Equation ([3.74](#S3.E74 "In 3.2.2 The general correlation case: A verification argument ‚Ä£ 3.2 Optimal strategy for the exponential utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) with Ōąi‚ąąC‚Äč([0,Tm‚Äča‚Äčx),‚ĄĚd)\psi^{i}\in C([0,T\_{max}),\mathbb{R}^{d}) in the sense that Ōąi\psi^{i} satisfies ([3.74](#S3.E74 "In 3.2.2 The general correlation case: A verification argument ‚Ä£ 3.2 Optimal strategy for the exponential utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) on [0,Tm‚Äča‚Äčx)[0,T\_{max}) with Tm‚Äča‚Äčx‚ąą(0,T]T\_{max}\in(0,T] and supt<Tm‚Äča‚Äčx|Ōąi‚Äč(t)|=+‚ąě\sup\_{t<T\_{max}}|\psi^{i}(t)|=+\infty, if Tm‚Äča‚Äčx<TT\_{max}<T.
Combining the component-wise solutions, we finally obtain the existence of a unique non-continuable solution Ōą‚ąąC‚Äč([0,Tm‚Äča‚Äčx),‚ĄĚd)\psi\in C([0,T\_{max}),\mathbb{R}^{d}) of the inhomogeneous Ricatti‚ÄďVolterra Equation ([3.43](#S3.E43 "In Proposition 3.6. ‚Ä£ 3.1.2 The general correlation case: A verification argument ‚Ä£ 3.1 Optimal strategy for the power utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models"))- ([3.44](#S3.E44 "In Proposition 3.6. ‚Ä£ 3.1.2 The general correlation case: A verification argument ‚Ä£ 3.1 Optimal strategy for the power utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) (and in particular of ([3.34](#S3.E34 "In Proposition 3.4. ‚Ä£ 3.1.1 The degenerate correlation case ‚Ä£ 3.1 Optimal strategy for the power utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models"))‚Äď ([3.35](#S3.E35 "In Proposition 3.4. ‚Ä£ 3.1.1 The degenerate correlation case ‚Ä£ 3.1 Optimal strategy for the power utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) ).

Note that our candidate for the optimal portfolio strategy őĪ‚ąó\alpha^{\*} is given, using ([3.39](#S3.E39 "In Theorem 3.5. ‚Ä£ 3.1.1 The degenerate correlation case ‚Ä£ 3.1 Optimal strategy for the power utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models"))‚Äď ([3.40](#S3.E40 "In Theorem 3.5. ‚Ä£ 3.1.1 The degenerate correlation case ‚Ä£ 3.1 Optimal strategy for the power utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")), by

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | őĪt‚ąó=11‚ąíő≥‚Äč(őĽt+ő£‚Äčőõt)=(11‚ąíő≥‚Äč(őłi+ŌĀi‚ÄčőĹi‚ÄčŌāi‚Äč(t)‚ÄčŌąi‚Äč(T‚ąít))‚ÄčVti)1‚Č§i‚Č§d,‚ÄĄ0‚Č§t‚Č§T.\alpha\_{t}^{\*}=\frac{1}{1-\gamma}\left(\lambda\_{t}+\Sigma\Lambda\_{t}\right)=\;\Big(\frac{1}{1-\gamma}\big(\theta\_{i}+\rho\_{i}\nu\_{i}\varsigma^{i}(t)\psi^{i}(T-t)\big)\sqrt{V\_{t}^{i}}\Big)\_{1\leq i\leq d},\;0\leq t\leq T. |  | (3.49) |

We will show directly that the corresponding value attained by this portfolio strategy is x0ő≥ő≥‚Äčőď0\frac{x\_{0}^{\gamma}}{\gamma}\Gamma\_{0} and every other admissible portfolio strategy will not yield a larger value. Then we have the following verification result:

###### Theorem 3.7.

Moreover,

|  |  |  |  |

and őĪ‚ąó\alpha^{\*} is admissible. The value function defined in ([3.33](#S3.E33 "In 3.1 Optimal strategy for the power utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) can be written as

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | supőĪ‚ąąūĚíúūĚĒľx0,V0‚Äč[(XTőĪ‚ąó)ő≥ő≥]=ūĚíĪ‚Äč(x0,V0)=x0ő≥ő≥‚Äčexp‚Ā°(ő≥‚Äč‚ąę0Tr‚Äč(s)‚ÄčūĚĎĎs+‚ąĎi=1d‚ąę0T(ő≥‚Äčőłi22‚Äč(1‚ąíő≥)+Fi‚Äč(s,Ōą‚Äč(T‚ąís)))‚Äčg0i‚Äč(s)‚ÄčūĚĎĎs).\sup\_{\alpha\in\mathcal{A}}\mathbb{E}\_{x\_{0},V\_{0}}\left[\frac{\big(X\_{T}^{\alpha^{\*}}\big)^{\gamma}}{\gamma}\right]=\mathcal{V}(x\_{0},V\_{0})=\frac{x\_{0}^{\gamma}}{\gamma}\exp\Big(\gamma\int\_{0}^{T}r(s)ds+\sum\_{i=1}^{d}\int\_{0}^{T}\big(\frac{\gamma\theta\_{i}^{2}}{2(1-\gamma)}+F\_{i}(s,\psi(T-s))\big)g^{i}\_{0}(s)ds\Big). |  |

For the sake of space limitation, but without loss of self-containedness, we present a sketch of the proof here.

*Sketch of Proof:*
In order to prove that őĪ‚ąó\alpha^{\*} is indeed the optimal portfolio strategy, we show that for

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | G‚Äč(x0,V0):=x0ő≥ő≥‚Äčőď0=x0ő≥ő≥‚Äčexp‚Ā°(ő≥‚Äč‚ąę0Tr‚Äč(s)‚ÄčūĚĎĎs+‚ąĎi=1d‚ąę0T(ő≥‚Äčőłi22‚Äč(1‚ąíő≥)+Fi‚Äč(s,Ōą‚Äč(T‚ąís)))‚Äčg0i‚Äč(s)‚ÄčūĚĎĎs),G(x\_{0},V\_{0}):=\frac{x\_{0}^{\gamma}}{\gamma}\Gamma\_{0}=\frac{x\_{0}^{\gamma}}{\gamma}\exp\Big(\gamma\int\_{0}^{T}r(s)ds+\sum\_{i=1}^{d}\int\_{0}^{T}\big(\frac{\gamma\theta\_{i}^{2}}{2(1-\gamma)}+F\_{i}(s,\psi(T-s))\big)g^{i}\_{0}(s)ds\Big), |  |

we have

1. 1.

   ūĚĒľx0,V0‚Äč[(XTőĪ‚ąó)ő≥ő≥]=G‚Äč(x0,V0)\mathbb{E}\_{x\_{0},V\_{0}}{\big[\frac{(X\_{T}^{\alpha^{\*}})^{\gamma}}{\gamma}\big]}=G(x\_{0},V\_{0}) for őĪt‚ąó=őĽt+ő£‚Äčőõt1‚ąíő≥=(11‚ąíő≥‚Äč(őłi+ŌĀi‚ÄčőĹi‚ÄčŌāi‚Äč(t)‚ÄčŌąi‚Äč(T‚ąít))‚ÄčVti)1‚Č§i‚Č§d,t‚ąą[0,T]\alpha\_{t}^{\*}=\frac{\lambda\_{t}+\Sigma\Lambda\_{t}}{1-\gamma}=\Big(\frac{1}{1-\gamma}\big(\theta\_{i}+\rho\_{i}\nu\_{i}\varsigma^{i}(t)\psi^{i}(T-t)\big)\sqrt{V\_{t}^{i}}\Big)\_{1\leq i\leq d},\;t\in[0,T],
2. 2.

   ūĚĒľx0,V0‚Äč[(XTőĪ)ő≥ő≥]‚Č§G‚Äč(x0,V0)\mathbb{E}\_{x\_{0},V\_{0}}{\big[\frac{(X\_{T}^{\alpha})^{\gamma}}{\gamma}\big]}\leq G(x\_{0},V\_{0}) for every other admissible strategy őĪ‚ąąūĚíú\alpha\in\mathcal{A}.

In fact, inserting the candidate őĪ‚ąó\alpha^{\*} for the
optimal portfolio strategy in the SDE of the wealth equation show by (1)(1) that the upper bound GG can be obtained. Consequently conditions (1)(1) and (2)(2) ensure that GG is the value function of the problem ([3.33](#S3.E33 "In 3.1 Optimal strategy for the power utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) and őĪ‚ąó\alpha^{\*} is the optimal portfolio strategy.

### 3.2 Optimal strategy for the exponential utility maximization problem

In this subsection, we consider the exponential utility case.
With a slightly different formulation, let ŌÄt\pi\_{t} denote the vector of the amounts invested in the risky assets SS at time tt in a self‚Äďfinancing strategy. We assume that the the process (ŌÄt)t‚Č•0(\pi\_{t})\_{t\geq 0} are progressively measurable. Then, the dynamics of the wealth XŌÄX^{\pi} of the portfolio we seek to optimize is given by

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | d‚ÄčXtŌÄ\displaystyle\mathrm{d}X^{\pi}\_{t} | =(ŌÄt‚ä§‚Äč(r‚Äč(t)‚ÄčūĚüôd+ŌÉ‚Äč(Vt)‚ÄčőĽt)+(XtŌÄ‚ąíŌÄt‚ä§‚ÄčūĚüôd)‚Äčr‚Äč(t))‚Äčd‚Äčt+ŌÄt‚ä§‚ÄčŌÉ‚Äč(Vt)‚Äčd‚ÄčBt\displaystyle=\bigl(\pi\_{t}^{\top}\big(r(t){\mathbb{1}\_{d}}+\sigma(V\_{t})\lambda\_{t}\big)+(X^{\pi}\_{t}-\pi\_{t}^{\top}{\mathbb{1}\_{d}})r(t)\bigr)\,\mathrm{d}t+\pi\_{t}^{\top}\sigma(V\_{t})\,\mathrm{d}B\_{t} |  |
|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  |  | =XtŌÄ‚Äč(r‚Äč(t)+ŌÄt‚ä§‚ÄčŌÉ‚Äč(Vt)‚ÄčőĽt)‚Äčd‚Äčt+ŌÄt‚ä§‚ÄčŌÉ‚Äč(Vt)‚Äčd‚ÄčBt=XtŌÄ‚Äč(r‚Äč(t)+ŌÄt‚ä§‚Äčdiag‚Ā°(Vt)‚Äčőł)‚Äčd‚Äčt+ŌÄt‚ä§‚Äčdiag‚Ā°(Vt)‚Äčd‚ÄčBt,\displaystyle=X^{\pi}\_{t}\bigl(r(t)+\pi\_{t}^{\top}\sigma(V\_{t})\lambda\_{t}\bigr)\,\mathrm{d}t+\pi\_{t}^{\top}\sigma(V\_{t})\,\mathrm{d}B\_{t}=X\_{t}^{\pi}(r(t)+\pi\_{t}^{\top}{\operatorname{diag}(V\_{t})}{\theta})dt+\pi\_{t}^{\top}\sqrt{\operatorname{diag}(V\_{t})}dB\_{t}, |  |

Letting őĪt:=ŌÉ‚ä§‚Äč(Vt)‚ÄčŌÄt\alpha\_{t}:=\sigma^{\top}(V\_{t})\pi\_{t} be the investment strategy, the wealth XőĪX^{\alpha} reads:

|  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | d‚ÄčXtőĪ\displaystyle dX^{\alpha}\_{t} | =(r‚Äč(t)‚ÄčXtőĪ+őĪt‚ä§‚ÄčőĽt)‚Äčd‚Äčt+őĪt‚ä§‚Äčd‚ÄčBt,t‚Č•0,X0őĪ=x0‚ąą‚ĄĚ.\displaystyle=\big(r(t)X^{\alpha}\_{t}+\alpha\_{t}^{\top}\lambda\_{t}\big)dt+\alpha\_{t}^{\top}dB\_{t},\quad t\geq 0,\quad X\_{0}^{\alpha}=x\_{0}\in\mathbb{R}. |  | (3.53) |

By a standard calculation, the wealth process is then given by

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | Xt=e‚ąę0tr‚Äč(s)‚ÄčūĚĎĎs‚Äč(x0+‚ąę0te‚ąí‚ąę0sr‚Äč(u)‚ÄčūĚĎĎu‚Äč(őĪs‚ä§‚Äčd‚ÄčBs+őĪs‚ä§‚ÄčőĽs‚Äčd‚Äčs)),X\_{t}=e^{\int^{t}\_{0}r(s)ds}\left(x\_{0}+\int\_{0}^{t}e^{-\int^{s}\_{0}r(u)du}\left(\alpha\_{s}^{\top}dB\_{s}+\alpha\_{s}^{\top}\lambda\_{s}\mathrm{d}s\right)\right), |  | (3.54) |

Note that it is sufficient to assume that ‚ąę0t(|őĽs|2+|őĪs|2)‚Äčds<+‚ąě\int\_{0}^{t}(\left|\lambda\_{s}\right|^{2}+\left|\alpha\_{s}\right|^{2})\,\mathrm{d}s<+\infty almost surely for all t‚Č•0t\geq 0
in order to construct the stochastic integrals in Equation ([3.54](#S3.E54 "In 3.2 Optimal strategy for the exponential utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")). This boundedness condition holds owing to the inequality |z|2‚Č§2‚Äče|z|,‚ąÄz‚ąą‚ĄĚ|z|^{2}\leq 2e^{|z|},\,\forall z\in\mathbb{R}, together with the condition ([3.27](#S3.E27 "In 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")), and the following admissibility assumption, which is consistent with Hu et al. ([2005](#bib.bib21)).

###### Definition 3.8.

Let ő≥>0\gamma>0, an investment strategy őĪ‚Äč(‚čÖ)\alpha(\cdot) is said to be admissible if

1. (a)(a)

   őĪ‚Äč(‚čÖ)\alpha(\cdot) is ūĚĒĹ\mathbb{F}-adapted and ūĚĒľ‚Äč[‚ąę0T|őĪs|2‚ÄčūĚĎĎs]<‚ąě\mathbb{E}[\int^{T}\_{0}\left|\alpha\_{s}\right|^{2}ds]<\infty;
2. (b)(b)

   The wealth process ([3.53](#S3.E53 "In 3.2 Optimal strategy for the exponential utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) has a unique solution in terms of (S,V,B)(S,V,B), with ‚Ąô\mathbb{P}-a.s. continuous paths;
3. (c)(c)

   {exp‚Ā°[‚ąíő≥‚Äče‚ąęŌĄTr‚Äč(u)‚ÄčūĚĎĎu‚ÄčXŌĄ]:ŌĄ‚Äč¬†stopping time with values in¬†‚Äč[0,T]}\left\{\exp\big[-\gamma e^{\int^{T}\_{\tau}r(u)du}X\_{\tau}\big]:\tau\text{ stopping time with values in }[0,T]\right\} is a uniformly integrable family.

In particular,

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | supŌĄ‚ąą[0,T]ūĚĒľ‚Äč[exp‚Ā°(‚ąíp‚Äčő≥‚Äče‚ąęŌĄTr‚Äč(u)‚ÄčūĚĎĎu‚ÄčXŌĄőĪ)]<‚ąě,¬†for some¬†‚Äčp>1.\sup\_{\tau\in[0,T]}\mathbb{E}\Big[\exp\left(-p\gamma e^{\int^{T}\_{\tau}r(u)du}X^{\alpha}\_{\tau}\right)\Big]<\infty,\text{ for some }p>1. |  | (3.55) |

The set of all admissible investment strategies is denoted as ūĚíú{\mathcal{A}} and is naturally defined by

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | ūĚíú={őĪ‚ąąLūĚĒĹ2,l‚Äčo‚Äčc‚Äč([0,T],‚ĄĚd)‚Äč¬†such that ([3.53](#S3.E53 "In 3.2 Optimal strategy for the exponential utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) has a solution satisfying condition¬†‚Äč([3.55](#S3.E55 "In Definition 3.8. ‚Ä£ 3.2 Optimal strategy for the exponential utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models"))}.\mathcal{A}=\{\alpha\in{L^{2,loc}\_{\mathbb{F}}([0,T],\mathbb{R}^{d})}\mbox{ such that \eqref{eq:wealth} has a solution satisfying condition }\penalty 10000\ \eqref{eq:uniformInt}\}. |  |

The investor now considers the Merton exponential utility optimization problem, i.e. its aim is to find the value function ūĚíĪ‚Äč(x0,V0)\mathcal{V}(x\_{0},V\_{0}) for the CARA utility function such that

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | ūĚíĪ‚Äč(x0,V0)=supőĪ‚Äč(‚čÖ)‚ąąūĚíúūĚĒľx0,V0‚Äč[‚ąí1ő≥‚Äčexp‚Ā°(‚ąíő≥‚ÄčXT)],ő≥>0.\mathcal{V}(x\_{0},V\_{0})=\sup\_{\alpha(\cdot)\in{\mathcal{A}}}\mathbb{E}\_{x\_{0},V\_{0}}\left[-\frac{1}{\gamma}\exp\Big(-\gamma X\_{T}\Big)\right],\quad\gamma>0. |  | (3.56) |

The solution method is similar to the power utility case. With slightly abuse of notations, we still use Ōą‚Äč(‚čÖ)\psi(\cdot), őď\Gamma, etc. However, they are redefined and not mixed with counterparts in power utility case.

#### 3.2.1 The degenerate correlation case

We assume that the correlation in ([2.15](#S2.E15 "In 2.2 Formulation of the stochastic Market model ‚Ä£ 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) is of the form (ŌĀ,‚Ä¶,ŌĀ)(\rho,\dots,\rho) for ŌĀ‚ąą[‚ąí1,1]\rho\in[-1,1]. To construct the family of processes {JtőĪ}t‚ąą[0,T]\{J^{\alpha}\_{t}\}\_{t\in[0,T]}, őĪ‚ąąūĚíú\alpha\in{\mathcal{A}}, satisfying conditions (1)(1)- (2)(2)- (3)(3) in Definition [3.2](#S3.ThmTheorem2 "Definition 3.2 (Martingale optimality principle). ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models"), we introduce the new probability measure ‚Ąô~\tilde{\mathbb{P}} defined via the Radon-Nikodym density or derivative at ‚ĄĪT\mathcal{F}\_{T} from

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | d‚Äč‚Ąô~d‚Äč‚Ąô|‚ĄĪt=‚Ąį‚Äč(‚ąí‚ąę0t‚ąĎi=1dőłi‚ÄčVsi‚Äčd‚ÄčBsi)=exp‚Ā°(‚ąí‚ąę0tőĽs‚ä§‚ÄčūĚĎĎBs‚ąí12‚Äč‚ąę0t|őĽs|2‚ÄčūĚĎĎs)\frac{d\tilde{\mathbb{P}}}{d\mathbb{P}}|\_{\mathcal{F}\_{t}}=\mathcal{E}\Big(-\int\_{0}^{t}\sum\_{i=1}^{d}\theta\_{i}\sqrt{V^{i}\_{s}}dB^{i}\_{s}\Big)=\operatorname{exp}\Big(-\int\_{0}^{t}\lambda\_{s}^{\top}dB\_{s}-\frac{1}{2}\int\_{0}^{t}\left|\lambda\_{s}\right|^{2}ds\Big) |  |

where the stochastic exponential is a true martingale by Lemma [5.1](#S5.ThmTheorem1 "Lemma 5.1 (Martingale property of stochastic exponentials). ‚Ä£ 5 Proofs of the main results ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models") together with the new standard brownian motion under ‚Ąô~\tilde{\mathbb{P}} , B~t=Bt+‚ąę0tőĽs‚ÄčūĚĎĎs.\widetilde{B}\_{t}=B\_{t}+\int\_{0}^{t}\lambda\_{s}ds.
Define the new process W~\widetilde{W} by

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | W~t=ő£‚ÄčB~t+I‚ąíő£‚ä§‚Äčő£‚ÄčBt‚üā=Wt+‚ąę0tő£‚ÄčőĽs‚ÄčūĚĎĎs,\widetilde{W}\_{t}=\Sigma\widetilde{B}\_{t}+\sqrt{I-\Sigma^{\top}\Sigma}B^{\perp}\_{t}=W\_{t}+\int\_{0}^{t}\Sigma\lambda\_{s}ds, |  |

Notice that, by the Girsanov theorem, B~\widetilde{B} and W~\widetilde{W} are standard Wiener processes under the measure ‚Ąô~\tilde{\mathbb{P}}.
As in the one dimensional case (see e.g. Han and Wong ([2020](#bib.bib19))), the Ansatz

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | JtőĪ=‚ąí1ő≥exp(‚ąíő≥e‚ąętTr‚Äč(s)‚ÄčūĚĎĎsXtőĪ)(ūĚĒľ‚Ąô~[exp(‚ąí1‚ąíŌĀ22‚ąętT|őĽs|2ds)|‚ĄĪt])11‚ąíŌĀ2=:‚ąí1ő≥exp(‚ąíő≥e‚ąętTr‚Äč(s)‚ÄčūĚĎĎsXtőĪ)őďt.J\_{t}^{\alpha}=-\frac{1}{\gamma}\exp\big(-\gamma e^{\int\_{t}^{T}r(s)ds}X^{\alpha}\_{t}\big)\Big(\mathbb{E}^{\tilde{\mathbb{P}}}\Big[\operatorname{exp}\big(-\frac{1-\rho^{2}}{2}\int\_{t}^{T}\left|\lambda\_{s}\right|^{2}ds\big)|\mathcal{F}\_{t}\Big]\Big)^{\frac{1}{1-\rho^{2}}}=:-\frac{1}{\gamma}\exp\big(-\gamma e^{\int\_{t}^{T}r(s)ds}X^{\alpha}\_{t}\big)\Gamma\_{t}. |  |

is inspired by the martingale distortion transformation in a non-Markovian setting in Tehranchi ([2004](#bib.bib30)) for the case of the
exponential utility function, where the distortion
power arises from simple H√∂lder-type inequalities.
Here we still use the short notation JtőĪJ\_{t}^{\alpha} for Jt‚Äč(XtőĪ,Vt)J\_{t}(X\_{t}^{\alpha},V\_{t}).

###### Proposition 3.9.

Assume that there exists a solution Ōą‚ąąC‚Äč([0,T],‚ĄĚd)\psi\in C([0,T],\mathbb{R}^{d}) to the inhomogeneous Riccati-Volterra equation ([3.57](#S3.E57 "In Proposition 3.9. ‚Ä£ 3.2.1 The degenerate correlation case ‚Ä£ 3.2 Optimal strategy for the exponential utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models"))-([3.58](#S3.E58 "In Proposition 3.9. ‚Ä£ 3.2.1 The degenerate correlation case ‚Ä£ 3.2 Optimal strategy for the exponential utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) below:

|  |  |  |  |  |

|  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | Fi‚Äč(s,Ōą)\displaystyle F\_{i}(s,\psi) | =‚ąíŌĀ‚Äčőłi‚ÄčőĹi‚ÄčŌāi‚Äč(s)‚ÄčŌąi+(D‚ä§‚ÄčŌą)i+őĹi22‚Äč(1‚ąíŌĀ2)‚Äč(Ōāi‚Äč(s)‚ÄčŌąi)2,i=1,‚Ä¶,d,\displaystyle=-\rho\theta\_{i}\nu\_{i}\varsigma^{i}(s)\psi^{i}+(D^{\top}\psi)\_{i}+\frac{\nu\_{i}^{2}}{2}(1-\rho^{2})(\varsigma^{i}(s)\psi^{i})^{2},\quad i=1,\ldots,d, |  | (3.58) |

Then,

|  |  |  |  |

|  | őďt=exp‚Ā°(‚ąĎi=1d‚ąętT(‚ąíőłi22+Fi‚Äč(s,Ōą‚Äč(T‚ąís)))‚Äčg~ti‚Äč(s)‚ÄčūĚĎĎs).\Gamma\_{t}=\exp\Big(\sum\_{i=1}^{d}\int\_{t}^{T}\big(-\frac{\theta\_{i}^{2}}{2}+F\_{i}(s,\psi(T-s))\big)\tilde{g}^{i}\_{t}(s)ds\Big). |  | (3.59) |

where g~=(g~1,‚Ä¶,g~d)‚ä§\tilde{g}=(\tilde{g}^{1},\ldots,\tilde{g}^{d})^{\top} is the ‚ĄĚd\mathbb{R}^{d}-valued process (g~t‚Äč(s))t‚Č§s(\tilde{g}\_{t}(s))\_{t\leq s} denoting the adjusted conditional ‚Ąô~\tilde{\mathbb{P}}-expected variance.
Moreover, őďt\Gamma\_{t} is essentially bounded. Specifically, 0<őďt‚Č§10<\Gamma\_{t}\leq 1, ‚ąÄt‚ąą[0,T]\forall\;t\in[0,T], ‚Ąô\mathbb{P}-a.s..

|  |  |  |  |

Moreover, (őď,őõ)‚ąąūĚēäūĚĒĹ‚ąě‚Äč([0,T],‚ĄĚ)√óLūĚĒĹ2‚Äč([0,T],‚ĄĚd)\left(\Gamma,\Lambda\right)\in\mathbb{S}^{\infty}\_{\mathbb{F}}([0,T],\mathbb{R})\times L^{2}\_{\mathbb{F}}([0,T],\mathbb{R}^{d}) and

|  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | d‚Äčőďt\displaystyle d\Gamma\_{t} | =őďt‚Äč(‚ąĎi=1d(őłi22+őĹi22‚ÄčŌĀ2‚Äč(Ōāi‚Äč(t)‚ÄčŌąi‚Äč(T‚ąít))2)‚ÄčVti+‚ąĎi=1dŌąi‚Äč(T‚ąít)‚ÄčőĹi‚ÄčŌāi‚Äč(t)‚ÄčVti‚Äčd‚ÄčW~ti)\displaystyle=\;\Gamma\_{t}\Big(\sum\_{i=1}^{d}\Big(\frac{\theta\_{i}^{2}}{2}+\frac{\nu\_{i}^{2}}{2}\rho^{2}(\varsigma^{i}(t)\psi^{i}(T-t))^{2}\Big)V^{i}\_{t}+\sum\_{i=1}^{d}\psi^{i}(T-t)\nu\_{i}\varsigma^{i}(t)\sqrt{V^{i}\_{t}}d\widetilde{W}^{i}\_{t}\Big) |  | (3.61) |

Remark

The main result we provide for this case is the following:

###### Theorem 3.10.

on the interval [0,T][0,T], such that Assumption [3.1](#S3.Thmassumption1 "Assumption 3.1. ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models") is in force. |  |  |  |  |  |

and őĪ‚ąó\alpha^{\*} is admissible.

#### 3.2.2 The general correlation case: A verification argument

As developed in the previous section, when the correlation structure is highly degenerate, that is, when
ŌĀ1=‚Ä¶=ŌĀd\rho\_{1}=\ldots=\rho\_{d}, the martingale distortion approach used by Han and Wong ([2020](#bib.bib19)) in the one-dimensional case extends naturally to the multivariate setting.
When the correlation structure in ([2.15](#S2.E15 "In 2.2 Formulation of the stochastic Market model ‚Ä£ 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) is given by an arbitrary vector
(ŌĀ1,‚Ä¶,ŌĀd)‚ąą[‚ąí1,1]d(\rho\_{1},\dots,\rho\_{d})\in[-1,1]^{d}, we rewrite the Riccati‚ÄďVolterra equations
([3.57](#S3.E57 "In Proposition 3.9. ‚Ä£ 3.2.1 The degenerate correlation case ‚Ä£ 3.2 Optimal strategy for the exponential utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models"))‚Äď([3.58](#S3.E58 "In Proposition 3.9. ‚Ä£ 3.2.1 The degenerate correlation case ‚Ä£ 3.2 Optimal strategy for the exponential utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) as

|  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | Ōąi‚Äč(t)\displaystyle\psi^{i}(t) | =‚ąę0tKi‚Äč(t‚ąís)‚Äč(‚ąíőłi22+Fi‚Äč(T‚ąís,Ōą‚Äč(s)))‚ÄčūĚĎĎs,\displaystyle=\int\_{0}^{t}K\_{i}(t-s)\Big(-\frac{\theta\_{i}^{2}}{2}+F\_{i}(T-s,\psi(s))\Big)\,ds, |  | (3.66) |
|  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | Fi‚Äč(s,Ōą)\displaystyle F\_{i}(s,\psi) | =‚ąíőłi‚ÄčŌĀi‚ÄčőĹi‚ÄčŌāi‚Äč(s)‚ÄčŌąi+(D‚ä§‚ÄčŌą)i+őĹi22‚Äč(1‚ąíŌĀi2)‚Äč(Ōāi‚Äč(s)‚ÄčŌąi)2,i=1,‚Ä¶,d.\displaystyle=-\theta\_{i}\rho\_{i}\nu\_{i}\varsigma^{i}(s)\psi^{i}+(D^{\top}\psi)\_{i}+\frac{\nu\_{i}^{2}}{2}(1-\rho\_{i}^{2})\big(\varsigma^{i}(s)\psi^{i}\big)^{2},\quad i=1,\ldots,d. |  | (3.67) |

First, note that if KiK\_{i} satisfies the Assumption [2.1](#S2.Thmassumption1 "Assumption 2.1 (On Volterra Equations with convolutive kernels). ‚Ä£ 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models") for i=1,‚Ä¶,di=1,\ldots,d. As 1‚ąíŌĀi2‚Č•01-\rho\_{i}^{2}\geq 0, then (Gnabeyeu, [2026](#bib.bib14), Theorem A.1) provides the existence of a unique global continuous solution on [0,T][0,T] to ([3.66](#S3.E66 "In 3.2.2 The general correlation case: A verification argument ‚Ä£ 3.2 Optimal strategy for the exponential utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models"))‚Äď ([3.67](#S3.E67 "In 3.2.2 The general correlation case: A verification argument ‚Ä£ 3.2 Optimal strategy for the exponential utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")). More details are given in the Remark on Proposition [3.11](#S3.ThmTheorem11 "Proposition 3.11. ‚Ä£ 3.2.2 The general correlation case: A verification argument ‚Ä£ 3.2 Optimal strategy for the exponential utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models").
In particular, when ŌĀ1=‚Ä¶=ŌĀd=ŌĀ\rho\_{1}=\ldots=\rho\_{d}=\rho, the function Ōą\psi coincides with the unique global solution to the Riccati‚ÄďVolterra equations ([3.57](#S3.E57 "In Proposition 3.9. ‚Ä£ 3.2.1 The degenerate correlation case ‚Ä£ 3.2 Optimal strategy for the exponential utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models"))‚Äď([3.58](#S3.E58 "In Proposition 3.9. ‚Ä£ 3.2.1 The degenerate correlation case ‚Ä£ 3.2 Optimal strategy for the exponential utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")).
Consequently, to avoid restrictions on the correlation structure, we still use a verification arguments in the spirit of B√§uerle and Li ([2013](#bib.bib6)) to solve the optimization problem, thus extending the results obtained in the preveous section to the more general correlation structure.

###### Proposition 3.11.

Assume that there exists a solution Ōą‚ąąC‚Äč([0,T],‚ĄĚd)\psi\in C([0,T],\mathbb{R}^{d}) to the inhomogeneous Riccati-Volterra equation:

|  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | Ōąi‚Äč(t)\displaystyle\psi^{i}(t) | =‚ąę0tKi‚Äč(t‚ąís)‚Äč(‚ąíőłi22+Fi‚Äč(T‚ąís,Ōą‚Äč(s)))‚ÄčūĚĎĎs,\displaystyle=\int\_{0}^{t}K\_{i}(t-s)\big(-\frac{\theta\_{i}^{2}}{2}+F\_{i}(T-s,\psi(s))\big)ds, |  | (3.68) |
|  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | Fi‚Äč(s,Ōą)\displaystyle F\_{i}(s,\psi) | =‚ąíőłi‚ÄčŌĀi‚ÄčőĹi‚ÄčŌāi‚Äč(s)‚ÄčŌąi+(D‚ä§‚ÄčŌą)i+őĹi22‚Äč(1‚ąíŌĀi2)‚Äč(Ōāi‚Äč(s)‚ÄčŌąi)2,i=1,‚Ä¶,d,\displaystyle=-\theta\_{i}\rho\_{i}\nu\_{i}\varsigma^{i}(s)\psi^{i}+(D^{\top}\psi)\_{i}+\frac{\nu\_{i}^{2}}{2}(1-\rho^{2}\_{i})(\varsigma^{i}(s)\psi^{i})^{2},\quad i=1,\ldots,d, |  | (3.69) |

Let (őď,őõ)\left(\Gamma,\Lambda\right) be defined as

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | {őďt=exp‚Ā°(‚ąĎi=1d‚ąętT(‚ąíőłi22+Fi‚Äč(s,Ōą‚Äč(T‚ąís)))‚Äčgti‚Äč(s)‚ÄčūĚĎĎs),őõti=őĹi‚ÄčŌāi‚Äč(t)‚ÄčŌąi‚Äč(T‚ąít)‚ÄčVti,i=1,‚Ä¶,d,0‚Č§t‚Č§T,\left\{\begin{array}[]{ccl}\Gamma\_{t}&=&\exp\Big(\sum\_{i=1}^{d}\int\_{t}^{T}\big(-\frac{\theta\_{i}^{2}}{2}+F\_{i}(s,\psi(T-s))\big)g^{i}\_{t}(s)ds\Big),\\ \Lambda\_{t}^{i}&=&\nu\_{i}\varsigma^{i}(t)\psi^{i}(T-t)\sqrt{V^{i}\_{t}},\quad i=1,\ldots,d,\quad 0\leq t\leq T,\end{array}\right. |  | (3.70) |

where gg == (g1,‚Ä¶,gd)‚ä§(g^{1},\ldots,g^{d})^{\top} is given by ([2.19](#S2.E19 "In 2.2 Formulation of the stochastic Market model ‚Ä£ 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) i.e. the ‚ĄĚd\mathbb{R}^{d}-valued process (gt‚Äč(s))t‚Č§s(g\_{t}(s))\_{t\leq s} is defined in ([2.19](#S2.E19 "In 2.2 Formulation of the stochastic Market model ‚Ä£ 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")). Then, (őď,őõ)\left(\Gamma,\Lambda\right) is a ūĚēäūĚĒĹ‚ąě‚Äč([0,T],‚ĄĚ)√óLūĚĒĹ2‚Äč([0,T],‚ĄĚd)\mathbb{S}^{\infty}\_{\mathbb{F}}([0,T],\mathbb{R})\times L^{2}\_{\mathbb{F}}([0,T],\mathbb{R}^{d})-valued solution to the Riccati BSDE ([3.71](#S3.E71 "In Proposition 3.11. ‚Ä£ 3.2.2 The general correlation case: A verification argument ‚Ä£ 3.2 Optimal strategy for the exponential utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) below.

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | {d‚Äčőďtőďt=12‚Äč|őĽt+ő£‚Äčőõt|2‚Äčd‚Äčt+őõt‚ä§‚Äčd‚ÄčWt,őďT=1.\left\{\begin{array}[]{ccl}\frac{d\Gamma\_{t}}{\Gamma\_{t}}&=&\frac{1}{2}\left|\lambda\_{t}+\Sigma\Lambda\_{t}\right|^{2}\,dt+\Lambda\_{t}^{\top}dW\_{t},\\ \Gamma\_{T}&=&1.\end{array}\right. |  | (3.71) |

Moreover, őďt\Gamma\_{t} is essentially bounded. Specifically, 0<őďt‚Č§10<\Gamma\_{t}\leq 1 for all t‚ąą[0,T]t\in[0,T], ‚Ąô\mathbb{P}-a.s..

Proof:  The proof that (őď,őõ)\left(\Gamma,\Lambda\right) satisfy ([3.71](#S3.E71 "In Proposition 3.11. ‚Ä£ 3.2.2 The general correlation case: A verification argument ‚Ä£ 3.2 Optimal strategy for the exponential utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) is a straightforward adaptation of the arguments from the proof of Proposition [3.9](#S3.ThmTheorem9 "Proposition 3.9. ‚Ä£ 3.2.1 The degenerate correlation case ‚Ä£ 3.2 Optimal strategy for the exponential utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models"). It remains to show that 0<őďt‚Č§10<\Gamma\_{t}\leq 1 for all t‚ąą[0,T]t\in[0,T], ‚Ąô\mathbb{P}-a.s. and (őď,őõ)‚ąąūĚēäūĚĒĹ‚ąě‚Äč([0,T],‚ĄĚ)√óLūĚĒĹ2‚Äč([0,T],‚ĄĚd)\left(\Gamma,\Lambda\right)\in\mathbb{S}^{\infty}\_{\mathbb{F}}([0,T],\mathbb{R})\times L^{2}\_{\mathbb{F}}([0,T],\mathbb{R}^{d}). For this, define the process

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | Mt\displaystyle M\_{t} | =őďt‚Äčexp‚Ā°(‚ąí12‚Äč‚ąę0t|őĽs+ő£‚Äčőõs|2‚ÄčūĚĎĎs)=őďt‚Äčexp‚Ā°(‚ąí12‚Äč‚ąę0t‚ąĎi=1dVsi‚Äč(őłi+ŌĀi‚ÄčőĹi‚ÄčŌāi‚Äč(s)‚ÄčŌąi‚Äč(T‚ąís))2‚Äčd‚Äčs),t‚Č§T.\displaystyle=\Gamma\_{t}\exp\Big(-\frac{1}{2}\int\_{0}^{t}\left|\lambda\_{s}+\Sigma\Lambda\_{s}\right|^{2}ds\Big)=\Gamma\_{t}\exp\Big(-\frac{1}{2}\int\_{0}^{t}\sum\_{i=1}^{d}V^{i}\_{s}\big(\theta\_{i}+\rho\_{i}\nu\_{i}\varsigma^{i}(s)\psi^{i}(T-s)\big)^{2}ds\Big),\quad t\leq T. |  |

An application of It√ī‚Äôs formula combined with the dynamics ([3.71](#S3.E71 "In Proposition 3.11. ‚Ä£ 3.2.2 The general correlation case: A verification argument ‚Ä£ 3.2 Optimal strategy for the exponential utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) shows that d‚ÄčMt=Mt‚Äčőõt‚ä§‚Äčd‚ÄčWtdM\_{t}=M\_{t}\Lambda\_{t}^{\top}dW\_{t}, so that MM is a local martingale of the form

|  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | Mt\displaystyle M\_{t} | =‚Ąį‚Äč(‚ąę0tőõs‚ä§‚ÄčūĚĎĎWs)=‚Ąį‚Äč(‚ąę0t‚ąĎi=1dőĹi‚ÄčŌāi‚Äč(s)‚ÄčŌąi‚Äč(T‚ąís)‚ÄčVsi‚Äčd‚ÄčWsi).\displaystyle=\;\mathcal{E}\Big(\int\_{0}^{t}\Lambda\_{s}^{\top}dW\_{s}\Big)=\;\mathcal{E}\Big(\int\_{0}^{t}\sum\_{i=1}^{d}\nu\_{i}\varsigma^{i}(s)\psi^{i}(T-s)\sqrt{V^{i}\_{s}}dW^{i}\_{s}\Big). |  | (3.72) |

Since Ōą\psi is continuous, it is bounded; likewise, Ōā\varsigma is bounded. Therefore a straightforward application of Lemma [5.1](#S5.ThmTheorem1 "Lemma 5.1 (Martingale property of stochastic exponentials). ‚Ä£ 5 Proofs of the main results ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models") with g2=0g\_{2}=0 and g1,i‚Äč(s)=őĹi‚ÄčŌāi‚Äč(s)‚ÄčŌąi‚Äč(T‚ąís)‚ąąL‚ąě‚Äč(‚ĄĚ+,‚ĄĚ)g\_{1,i}(s)=\nu\_{i}\varsigma^{i}(s)\psi^{i}(T-s)\in L^{\infty}(\mathbb{R}^{+},\mathbb{R}), recall ([2.17](#S2.E17 "In Theorem 2.7. ‚Ä£ 2.2 Formulation of the stochastic Market model ‚Ä£ 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")), yields that the stochastic exponential MM is a true ‚Ąô\mathbb{P}- martingale. Now, as őďT=1\Gamma\_{T}=1, writing ūĚĒľ‚Äč[MT|‚ĄĪt]=Mt\mathbb{E}[M\_{T}|\mathcal{F}\_{t}]=M\_{t}, we obtain

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | őďt=ūĚĒľ‚Äč[exp‚Ā°(‚ąí12‚Äč‚ąętT‚ąĎi=1dVsi‚Äč(őłi+ŌĀi‚ÄčőĹi‚ÄčŌāi‚Äč(s)‚ÄčŌąi‚Äč(T‚ąís))2‚Äčd‚Äčs)‚ą£‚ĄĪt],t‚Č§T,\Gamma\_{t}=\mathbb{E}\Big[\exp\Big(-\frac{1}{2}\int\_{t}^{T}\sum\_{i=1}^{d}V^{i}\_{s}\big(\theta\_{i}+\rho\_{i}\nu\_{i}\varsigma^{i}(s)\psi^{i}(T-s)\big)^{2}ds\Big)\mid\mathcal{F}\_{t}\Big],\quad t\leq T, |  | (3.73) |

which ensures that 0<őďt‚Č§10<\Gamma\_{t}\leq 1, ‚Ąô‚ąía.s.\mathbb{P}-a.s., since VtV\_{t} is non-negative (V‚ąą‚ĄĚ+dV\in\mathbb{R}^{d}\_{+}). As for őõ\Lambda, it is clear that it belongs to LūĚĒĹ2‚Äč([0,T],‚ĄĚd)L^{2}\_{\mathbb{F}}([0,T],\mathbb{R}^{d}) since Ōā\varsigma and Ōą\psi are bounded, Ōą\psi is continuous thus bounded and ūĚĒľ‚Äč[‚ąę0T‚ąĎi=1dVsi‚Äčd‚Äčs]<‚ąě\mathbb{E}\Big[\int\_{0}^{T}\sum\_{i=1}^{d}V^{i}\_{s}ds\Big]<\infty by ([2.17](#S2.E17 "In Theorem 2.7. ‚Ä£ 2.2 Formulation of the stochastic Market model ‚Ä£ 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")). This complete the Proof ‚Ė°\Box

Remark:
Assume that KK satisfies the Assumption [2.1](#S2.Thmassumption1 "Assumption 2.1 (On Volterra Equations with convolutive kernels). ‚Ä£ 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models").
Then (Gnabeyeu, [2026](#bib.bib14), Theorem A.1) provides the existence of a unique global continuous solution Ōą‚ąąC‚Äč([0,T],‚ĄĚd)\psi\in C([0,T],\mathbb{R}^{d}) to ([3.68](#S3.E68 "In Proposition 3.11. ‚Ä£ 3.2.2 The general correlation case: A verification argument ‚Ä£ 3.2 Optimal strategy for the exponential utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models"))‚Äď ([3.69](#S3.E69 "In Proposition 3.11. ‚Ä£ 3.2.2 The general correlation case: A verification argument ‚Ä£ 3.2 Optimal strategy for the exponential utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) (and in particular to ([3.57](#S3.E57 "In Proposition 3.9. ‚Ä£ 3.2.1 The degenerate correlation case ‚Ä£ 3.2 Optimal strategy for the exponential utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models"))‚Äď ([3.58](#S3.E58 "In Proposition 3.9. ‚Ä£ 3.2.1 The degenerate correlation case ‚Ä£ 3.2 Optimal strategy for the exponential utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) ) and Ōą<0\psi<0 for t>0t>0.
More precisely, as the matrix DD in the drift of the volatility process is a diagonal matrix, i.e. D=‚ąídiag‚Ā°(őĽ1,‚Ä¶,őĽd)D=-\operatorname{diag}{(\lambda\_{1},\dots,\lambda\_{d})}, for i=1,‚Ä¶,d,i=1,\ldots,d, by (Gnabeyeu, [2026](#bib.bib14), Corollary A.2), since ‚ąíőłi22<0-\frac{\theta\_{i}^{2}}{2}<0, Ōąi‚ąąC‚Äč([0,T],‚ĄĚ‚ąí)\psi^{i}\in C([0,T],\mathbb{R}\_{-}) is unique global solution to the following Volterra equation

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | Ōá‚Äč(t)=‚ąę0tKi‚Äč(t‚ąís)‚Äč(‚ąíőłi22‚ąí(őĽi+őłi‚ÄčŌĀi‚ÄčőĹi‚ÄčŌāi‚Äč(T‚ąís))‚ÄčŌá‚Äč(s)+őĹi22‚Äč(1‚ąíŌĀi2)‚ÄčŌāi‚Äč(T‚ąís)2‚ÄčŌá‚Äč(s)2)‚ÄčūĚĎĎs,t‚Č§T.\chi(t)=\int\_{0}^{t}K\_{i}(t-s)\Big(-\frac{\theta\_{i}^{2}}{2}-\big(\lambda\_{i}+\theta\_{i}\rho\_{i}\nu\_{i}\varsigma^{i}(T-s)\big)\chi(s)+\frac{\nu\_{i}^{2}}{2}(1-\rho\_{i}^{2})\varsigma^{i}(T-s)^{2}\chi(s)^{2}\Big)ds,\;t\leq T. |  | (3.74) |

Moreover, it follows in this case that the condition ([3.25](#S3.E25 "In Assumption 3.1. ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) can be made more explicit by bounding Ōą\psi with respect to the vector őł\theta.
Indeed setting for i=1,‚Ä¶,d,i=1,\ldots,d, őĽ¬Įi:=inft‚ąą[0,T](őĽi+őĹi‚ÄčŌĀi‚Äčőłi‚ÄčŌāi‚Äč(t))=őĽi+őĹi‚ÄčŌĀi‚Äčőłi‚Äč‚ÄĖŌāi‚ÄĖ‚ąě‚ÄčūĚüôŌĀi‚Č§0,\bar{\lambda}\_{i}:=\inf\_{t\in[0,T]}\big(\lambda\_{i}+\nu\_{i}\rho\_{i}\theta\_{i}\varsigma^{i}(t)\big)=\lambda\_{i}+\nu\_{i}\rho\_{i}\theta\_{i}\|\varsigma^{i}\|\_{\infty}{\mathbb{1}\_{\rho\_{i}\leq 0}}, which is strictly positive, still by (Gnabeyeu, [2026](#bib.bib14), Corollary A.2), we have:

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | supt‚ąą[0,T]|Ōąi‚Äč(t)|‚Č§|őłi|22‚ÄčőĽ¬Įi‚Äč‚ąę0TfőĽ¬Įi‚Äč(s)‚ÄčūĚĎĎs=|őłi|22‚ÄčőĽ¬Įi‚Äč(1‚ąíRőĽ¬Įi‚Äč(T)),i=1,‚Ä¶,d.\sup\_{t\in[0,T]}|\psi^{i}(t)|\leq\frac{|\theta\_{i}|^{2}}{2\bar{\lambda}\_{i}}\int\_{0}^{T}f\_{\bar{\lambda}\_{i}}(s)ds=\frac{|\theta\_{i}|^{2}}{2\bar{\lambda}\_{i}}(1-R\_{\bar{\lambda}\_{i}}(T)),\;i=1,\ldots,d. |  | (3.75) |

|  |  |  |  |

|  | őłi2‚Äč(1+(őĹi‚Äč‚ÄĖŌāi‚ÄĖ‚ąě‚Äčőłi2‚ÄčőĽ¬Įi)2‚Äč(1‚ąíRőĽ¬Įi‚Äč(T))2)‚Č§aa‚Äč(p)for alli=1,‚Ä¶,d.\theta^{2}\_{i}\left(1+(\nu\_{i}\|\varsigma^{i}\|\_{\infty}\frac{\theta\_{i}}{2\bar{\lambda}\_{i}})^{2}\big(1-R\_{\bar{\lambda}\_{i}}(T)\big)^{2}\right)\leq\frac{a}{a(p)}\quad\text{for all}\quad i=1,\ldots,d. |  | (3.76) |

Now, observe that the proposed candidate for the optimal portfolio strategy őĪ‚ąó\alpha^{\*} follows from

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | őĪt‚ąó=1ő≥‚Äče‚ąí‚ąętTr‚Äč(s)‚ÄčūĚĎĎs‚Äč(őĽt+ő£‚Äčőõt)=(1ő≥‚Äče‚ąí‚ąętTr‚Äč(s)‚ÄčūĚĎĎs‚Äč(őłi+ŌĀi‚ÄčőĹi‚ÄčŌāi‚Äč(t)‚ÄčŌąi‚Äč(T‚ąít))‚ÄčVti)1‚Č§i‚Č§d,0‚Č§t‚Č§T.\alpha\_{t}^{\*}=\frac{1}{\gamma}e^{-\int\_{t}^{T}r(s)ds}\left(\lambda\_{t}+\Sigma\Lambda\_{t}\right)=\Bigg(\frac{1}{\gamma}e^{-\int\_{t}^{T}r(s)ds}\big(\theta\_{i}+\rho\_{i}\nu\_{i}\varsigma^{i}(t)\psi^{i}(T-t)\big)\sqrt{V\_{t}^{i}}\Bigg)\_{1\leq i\leq d},\quad 0\leq t\leq T. |  | (3.77) |

We will show directly that this strategy attains the value
‚ąí1ő≥‚Äčexp‚Ā°(‚ąíő≥‚Äče‚ąętTr‚Äč(s)‚ÄčūĚĎĎs‚Äčx0)‚Äčőď0-\frac{1}{\gamma}\exp\left(-\gamma e^{\int\_{t}^{T}r(s)ds}x\_{0}\right)\Gamma\_{0}, and that no other admissible portfolio
strategy can achieve a higher value.
The main verification result for this setting is stated as follows:

###### Theorem 3.12.

Let Ōą\psi be the unique, continuous solution of the inhomogeneous Ricatti-Volterra equation ([3.68](#S3.E68 "In Proposition 3.11. ‚Ä£ 3.2.2 The general correlation case: A verification argument ‚Ä£ 3.2 Optimal strategy for the exponential utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models"))- ([3.69](#S3.E69 "In Proposition 3.11. ‚Ä£ 3.2.2 The general correlation case: A verification argument ‚Ä£ 3.2 Optimal strategy for the exponential utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models"))
on the interval [0,T][0,T], such that Assumption [3.1](#S3.Thmassumption1 "Assumption 3.1. ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models") is in force.
Then for t‚ąą[0,T]t\in[0,T], an optimal investment strategy (őĪt‚ąó)t‚ąą[0,T](\alpha\_{t}^{\*})\_{t\in[0,T]} for the Merton portfolio problem ([3.56](#S3.E56 "In 3.2 Optimal strategy for the exponential utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) is given by

|  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | őĪt‚ąó\displaystyle\alpha^{\*}\_{t} | =1ő≥‚Äče‚ąí‚ąętTr‚Äč(s)‚ÄčūĚĎĎs‚Äč(őĽt+ő£‚Äčőõt)=1ő≥‚Äče‚ąí‚ąętTr‚Äč(s)‚ÄčūĚĎĎs‚Äčdiag‚Ā°(Vt)‚Äč(őł+ő£‚ÄčőĹ‚ÄčŌā‚Äč(t)‚ÄčŌą‚Äč(T‚ąít)),0‚Č§t‚Č§T\displaystyle=\frac{1}{\gamma}e^{-\int\_{t}^{T}r(s)ds}\left(\lambda\_{t}+\Sigma\Lambda\_{t}\right)=\frac{1}{\gamma}e^{-\int\_{t}^{T}r(s)ds}\sqrt{\operatorname{diag}(V\_{t})}\left(\theta+\Sigma\nu\varsigma(t)\psi(T-t)\right),\quad 0\leq t\leq T |  | (3.78) |
|  |  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  |  | =(1ő≥‚Äče‚ąí‚ąętTr‚Äč(s)‚ÄčūĚĎĎs‚Äč(őłi+ŌĀi‚ÄčőĹi‚ÄčŌāi‚Äč(t)‚ÄčŌąi‚Äč(T‚ąít))‚ÄčVti)1‚Č§i‚Č§d,0‚Č§t‚Č§T.\displaystyle=\;\Big(\frac{1}{\gamma}e^{-\int\_{t}^{T}r(s)ds}\big(\theta\_{i}+\rho\_{i}\nu\_{i}\varsigma^{i}(t)\psi^{i}(T-t)\big)\sqrt{V\_{t}^{i}}\Big)\_{1\leq i\leq d},\quad 0\leq t\leq T. |  | (3.79) |

Moreover,

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | supŌĄ‚ąą[0,T]ūĚĒľ‚Äč[exp‚Ā°(‚ąíp‚Äčő≥‚Äče‚ąęŌĄTr‚Äč(u)‚ÄčūĚĎĎu‚ÄčXŌĄőĪ‚ąó)]<‚ąě,¬†for some¬†‚Äčp>1.\sup\_{\tau\in[0,T]}\mathbb{E}\Big[\exp\left(-p\gamma e^{\int^{T}\_{\tau}r(u)du}X^{\alpha^{\*}}\_{\tau}\right)\Big]<\infty,\text{ for some }p>1. |  | (3.80) |

and őĪ‚ąó\alpha^{\*} is admissible. The value function defined in ([3.56](#S3.E56 "In 3.2 Optimal strategy for the exponential utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) can be written as

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | ūĚíĪ‚Äč(x0,V0)=‚ąí1ő≥‚Äčexp‚Ā°(‚ąíő≥‚Äče‚ąę0Tr‚Äč(s)‚ÄčūĚĎĎs‚Äčx0)‚Äčexp‚Ā°(‚ąĎi=1d‚ąę0T(‚ąíőłi22+Fi‚Äč(s,Ōą‚Äč(T‚ąís)))‚Äčg0i‚Äč(s)‚ÄčūĚĎĎs).\mathcal{V}(x\_{0},V\_{0})=-\frac{1}{\gamma}\exp\left(-\gamma e^{\int\_{0}^{T}r(s)ds}x\_{0}\right)\exp\Big(\sum\_{i=1}^{d}\int\_{0}^{T}\big(-\frac{\theta\_{i}^{2}}{2}+F\_{i}(s,\psi(T-s))\big)g^{i}\_{0}(s)ds\Big). |  | (3.81) |

For the sake of brevity, yet without compromising self-containment, we present a sketch of the proof here.

*Sketch of Proof:*
In order to prove that őĪ‚ąó\alpha^{\*} is indeed the optimal portfolio strategy, we show that for

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | G‚Äč(x0,V0):=‚ąíőď0ő≥‚Äčexp‚Ā°(‚ąíő≥‚Äče‚ąę0Tr‚Äč(s)‚ÄčūĚĎĎs‚Äčx0)=‚ąí1ő≥‚Äčexp‚Ā°(‚ąíő≥‚Äče‚ąę0Tr‚Äč(s)‚ÄčūĚĎĎs‚Äčx0+‚ąĎi=1d‚ąę0T(‚ąíőłi22+Fi‚Äč(s,Ōą‚Äč(T‚ąís)))‚Äčg0i‚Äč(s)‚ÄčūĚĎĎs)G(x\_{0},V\_{0}):=-\frac{\Gamma\_{0}}{\gamma}\exp\big(-\gamma e^{\int\_{0}^{T}r(s)ds}x\_{0}\big)=-\frac{1}{\gamma}\exp\big(-\gamma e^{\int\_{0}^{T}r(s)ds}x\_{0}+\sum\_{i=1}^{d}\int\_{0}^{T}\big(-\frac{\theta\_{i}^{2}}{2}+F\_{i}(s,\psi(T-s))\big)g^{i}\_{0}(s)ds\big) |  |

we have

1. 1.

   ūĚĒľx0,V0‚Äč[‚ąí1ő≥‚Äčexp‚Ā°(‚ąíő≥‚ÄčXTőĪ‚ąó)]=G‚Äč(x0,V0)\mathbb{E}\_{x\_{0},V\_{0}}{\big[-\frac{1}{\gamma}\exp\big(-\gamma X\_{T}^{\alpha^{\*}}\big)\big]}=G(x\_{0},V\_{0}) for őĪt‚ąó=1ő≥‚Äče‚ąí‚ąętTr‚Äč(s)‚ÄčūĚĎĎs‚Äč(őĽt+ő£‚Äčőõt),‚ÄĄ0‚Č§t‚Č§T\alpha\_{t}^{\*}=\frac{1}{\gamma}e^{-\int\_{t}^{T}r(s)ds}\left(\lambda\_{t}+\Sigma\Lambda\_{t}\right),\;0\leq t\leq T,
2. 2.

   ūĚĒľx0,V0‚Äč[‚ąí1ő≥‚Äčexp‚Ā°(‚ąíő≥‚ÄčXTőĪ)]‚Č§G‚Äč(x0,V0)\mathbb{E}\_{x\_{0},V\_{0}}{\big[-\frac{1}{\gamma}\exp\big(-\gamma X\_{T}^{\alpha}\big)\big]}\leq G(x\_{0},V\_{0}) for every other admissible strategy őĪ‚ąąūĚíú\alpha\in\mathcal{A}.

In fact, conditions (1)(1) and (2)(2) ensure that G is the value function of the problem ([3.56](#S3.E56 "In 3.2 Optimal strategy for the exponential utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) and őĪ‚ąó\alpha^{\*} is the optimal portfolio strategy.

## 4 Numerical experiments: The particular case of the fake stationary rough Heston volatility

In this section, we illustrate the results of Section [2](#S2 "2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models") by numerically computing the optimal portfolio strategy for a special case of two-dimensional fake stationary rough heston model model as described in section [3](#S3 "3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models"). We consider a financial market consisting of one risk-free asset and d=2d=2 risky assets, with an investment horizon of T=1T=1 year. To model the roughness of the asset price dynamics, we employ an appropriate integration kernel. We choose a fractional kernel of Remark [2.1](#S2.ThmTheorem1 "Remark 2.1. ‚Ä£ 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models") and Example [2.6](#S2.ThmTheorem6 "Example 2.6. ‚Ä£ 2.1 Stabilizer and fake stationarity regimes. ‚Ä£ 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models") of the form:

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | K‚Äč(t)=(tőĪ1‚ąí1őď‚Äč(őĪ1)00tőĪ2‚ąí1őď‚Äč(őĪ2)),0.4+12=őĪ1,‚ÄČ0.1+12=őĪ2‚ąą(12,1).K(t)=\begin{pmatrix}\frac{t^{\alpha\_{1}-1}}{\Gamma(\alpha\_{1})}&0\\ 0&\frac{t^{\alpha\_{2}-1}}{\Gamma(\alpha\_{2})}\end{pmatrix},\quad 0.4+\frac{1}{2}=\alpha\_{1},\,0.1+\frac{1}{2}=\alpha\_{2}\in\big(\frac{1}{2},1\big). |  |

Here, őď‚Äč(őĪ)\Gamma(\alpha) is the Gamma function, and the parameter őĪ\alpha controls the degree of roughness in the model.

Note that, the model is sufficiently rich to capture several well-known stylized facts of financial markets:

* ‚ÄĒ

  Each asset SiS^{i}, i=1,2i=1,2 exhibits stochastic rough volatility driven by the process ViV^{i}, with different Hurst indices őĪi\alpha\_{i}.
* ‚ÄĒ

  Each stock SiS^{i} is correlated with its own volatility process through the parameter ŌĀi\rho\_{i} to take into
  account the leverage effect.

We consider the setting where in Equation ([2.2](#S2.E2 "In 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")), the simplified specification
ŌÜ‚Äč(t)=I2√ó2,t‚Č•0,\varphi(t)=I\_{2\times 2},\;t\geq 0, holds almost surely, in which case the ‚ĄĚd‚ąí\mathbb{R}^{d}- valued mean-reverting function őľ\mu is constant in time, that is, őľ‚Äč(t)=őľ0‚ąą‚ĄĚ2,‚ąÄt‚Č•0,\mu(t)=\mu\_{0}\in\mathbb{R}^{2},\;\forall\,t\geq 0, (see, e.g., Gnabeyeu and Pag√®s ([2025](#bib.bib15))).

We consider the following estimates for the model parameters V0i‚ąľūĚí©‚Äč(őľ0iőĽi,v0i)V\_{0}^{i}\sim\mathcal{N}(\frac{\mu\_{0}^{i}}{\lambda\_{i}},v\_{0}^{i}) defined in ([2.12](#S2.E12 "In Proposition 2.4 (Fake stationary Volterra square root process.). ‚Ä£ 2.1 Stabilizer and fake stationarity regimes. ‚Ä£ 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) ((EőĽi,ciE\_{\lambda\_{i},c\_{i}})):

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | c=(0.010.03),őľ0=(0.20.25),D=(‚ąí0.200‚ąí0.6),ő£=(‚ąí0.700‚ąí0.55),őł=(0.10.1),őĹ=(0.40.2).c=\begin{pmatrix}0.01\\ 0.03\end{pmatrix},\quad\mu\_{0}=\begin{pmatrix}0.2\\ 0.25\end{pmatrix},\;D=\begin{pmatrix}-0.2&0\\ 0&-0.6\end{pmatrix},\quad\Sigma=\begin{pmatrix}-0.7&0\\ 0&-0.55\end{pmatrix},\;\theta=\begin{pmatrix}0.1\\ 0.1\end{pmatrix},\;\nu=\begin{pmatrix}0.4\\ 0.2\end{pmatrix}. |  |

Remark:
In order to numerically implement the optimal strategy ([3.51](#S3.E51 "In Theorem 3.7. ‚Ä£ 3.1.2 The general correlation case: A verification argument ‚Ä£ 3.1 Optimal strategy for the power utility ‚Ä£ 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) and to discretize the Riccati-Volterra Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models"))‚Äď ([3.44](#S3.E44 "In Proposition 3.6. ‚Ä£ 3.1.2 The general correlation case: A verification argument ‚Ä£ 3.1 Optimal strategy for the power utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) respectively.

### 4.1 About the numerical scheme for the Volterra and fractional Riccati equations

To simulate the Volterra process ([2.2](#S2.E2 "In 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models"))‚Äď([2.18](#S2.E18 "In 2.2 Formulation of the stochastic Market model ‚Ä£ 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")), we first rewrite it using the equivalent Wiener‚ÄďHopf transform (see, e.g., (Gnabeyeu and Pag√®s, [2025](#bib.bib15); Gnabeyeu et al., [a](#bib.bib16), Propositions 2.8 and 2.2)).
We then introduce the főĽf\_{\lambda}-integrated discrete time Euler-Maruyama scheme defined by the below equation on the time grid tk=tkn=k‚ÄčTn,k=0,‚Ä¶,nt\_{k}=t^{n}\_{k}=\frac{kT}{n},k=0,\dots,n and in the fractional kernel case, namely recursively for i=1,2i=1,2, V¬Į0i,n=Vi,0\;\overline{V}^{i,n}\_{0}=V^{i,0} and for every k=1,‚Ä¶,nk=1,\ldots,n,

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | V¬Įtki,n=őľ0iőĽi+(Vi,0‚ąíőľ0iőĽi)‚ÄčRőĽi‚Äč(tk)+őĹiőĽi‚Äč‚ąĎ‚Ąď=1kŌāi‚Äč(t‚Ąď)‚ÄčV¬Įt‚Ąď‚ąí1i,n‚Äč‚ąęt‚Ąď‚ąí1t‚ĄďfőĪi,őĽi‚Äč(tk‚ąís)‚ÄčūĚĎĎWs=hi‚Äč(tk)+őĹiőĽi‚Äč‚ąĎ‚Ąď=1kŌāi‚Äč(t‚Ąď)‚ÄčV¬Įt‚Ąď‚ąí1i,n‚ÄčIki,‚Ąď.\overline{V}^{i,n}\_{t\_{k}}=\frac{\mu\_{0}^{i}}{\lambda\_{i}}+\big(V^{i,0}-\frac{\mu\_{0}^{i}}{\lambda\_{i}}\big)R\_{\lambda\_{i}}(t\_{k})+\frac{\nu\_{i}}{\lambda\_{i}}\sum\_{\ell=1}^{k}\varsigma^{i}(t\_{\ell})\sqrt{\overline{V}\_{t\_{\ell-1}}^{i,n}}\int\_{t\_{\ell-1}}^{t\_{\ell}}f\_{\alpha\_{i},\lambda\_{i}}(t\_{k}-s)\,dW\_{s}=h^{i}(t\_{k})+\frac{\nu\_{i}}{\lambda\_{i}}\sum\_{\ell=1}^{k}\varsigma^{i}(t\_{\ell})\sqrt{\overline{V}\_{t\_{\ell-1}}^{i,n}}I^{i,\ell}\_{k}. |  |

where the stochastic integrals (Iki,‚Ąď=‚ąęt‚Ąď‚ąí1t‚ĄďfőĪi,őĽi‚Äč(tk‚ąís)‚ÄčūĚĎĎWs)\left(I^{i,\ell}\_{k}=\int\_{t\_{\ell-1}}^{t\_{\ell}}f\_{\alpha\_{i},\lambda\_{i}}(t\_{k}-s)\,dW\_{s}\right) can be simulated on the discrete grid (tkn)0‚Č§k‚Č§n(t^{n}\_{k})\_{0\leq k\leq n} by generating an independent sequence of gaussian vectors Gn,‚Ąď,‚Ąď=1‚Äč‚čĮ‚ÄčnG^{n,\ell},\ell=1\cdots n using an extended and stable version of Cholesky decomposition of a well-defined covariance matrix CC.
The reader is referred to (Gnabeyeu and Pag√®s, [2025](#bib.bib15), Appendix A) for further details about the simulation of the Gaussian stochastic integrals terms in the semi-integrated Euler scheme introduced in this context for Equation ([2.2](#S2.E2 "In 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models"))‚Äď ([2.18](#S2.E18 "In 2.2 Formulation of the stochastic Market model ‚Ä£ 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")).

To design an approximation scheme for solving the two-dimensional Riccati‚ÄďVolterra system of equations
([3.43](#S3.E43 "In Proposition 3.6. ‚Ä£ 3.1.2 The general correlation case: A verification argument ‚Ä£ 3.1 Optimal strategy for the power utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models"))‚Äď([3.44](#S3.E44 "In Proposition 3.6. ‚Ä£ 3.1.2 The general correlation case: A verification argument ‚Ä£ 3.1 Optimal strategy for the power utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) and
([3.68](#S3.E68 "In Proposition 3.11. ‚Ä£ 3.2.2 The general correlation case: A verification argument ‚Ä£ 3.2 Optimal strategy for the exponential utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models"))‚Äď([3.69](#S3.E69 "In Proposition 3.11. ‚Ä£ 3.2.2 The general correlation case: A verification argument ‚Ä£ 3.2 Optimal strategy for the exponential utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) numerically,
we employ as in (El Euch and Rosenbaum, [2019](#bib.bib11), section 5.1) the generalized Adams‚ÄďBashforth‚ÄďMoulton method, often referred to as the fractional Adams method investigated in Diethelm et al. ([2002](#bib.bib9), [2004](#bib.bib10)) as a useful numerical algorithm for solving a fractional ordinary differential equation (ODE) based on a predictor-corrector approach.

Over a regular or uniform discrete time-grid (tk)k=1,‚Ä¶,n(t\_{k})\_{k=1,\ldots,n} with mesh or step length őĒ=Tn\Delta=\frac{T}{n} (tk=k‚ÄčőĒ)(t\_{k}=k\Delta) for some integer nn, let yji:=Ōąi‚Äč(tj)y\_{j}^{i}:=\psi^{i}(t\_{j}), the explicit numerical scheme to estimate Ōą\psi is given by

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | {yk+1i,P=‚ąĎj=0kbj,k+1i‚Äčfi‚Äč(tj,yji),with‚Äčfi‚Äč(tj,x):=ai+Fi‚Äč(T‚ąítj,x)yk+1i=‚ąĎj=0kaj,k+1i‚Äčfi‚Äč(tj,yji)+ak+1,k+1i‚Äčfi‚Äč(tk+1,yk+1i,P),y0i=0,i‚ąą{1,2}.\begin{cases}y\_{k+1}^{i,P}=\displaystyle\sum\_{j=0}^{k}b^{i}\_{j,k+1}f\_{i}(t\_{j},y\_{j}^{i}),\;\text{with}\;f\_{i}(t\_{j},x):=a\_{i}+F\_{i}(T-t\_{j},x)\\ y\_{k+1}^{i}=\displaystyle\sum\_{j=0}^{k}a^{i}\_{j,k+1}f\_{i}(t\_{j},y\_{j}^{i})+a^{i}\_{k+1,k+1}f\_{i}(t\_{k+1},y\_{k+1}^{i,P}),\quad y\_{0}^{i}=0\end{cases},\;i\in\{1,2\}. |  |

where ai=ő≥‚Äčőłi22‚Äč(1‚ąíő≥)a\_{i}=\frac{\gamma\theta\_{i}^{2}}{2(1-\gamma)} in section [3.1](#S3.SS1 "3.1 Optimal strategy for the power utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models") (resp. ai=‚ąíőłi22a\_{i}=-\frac{\theta\_{i}^{2}}{2} in section [3.2](#S3.SS2 "3.2 Optimal strategy for the exponential utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")), FiF\_{i} in ([3.44](#S3.E44 "In Proposition 3.6. ‚Ä£ 3.1.2 The general correlation case: A verification argument ‚Ä£ 3.1 Optimal strategy for the power utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) (resp. in ([3.69](#S3.E69 "In Proposition 3.11. ‚Ä£ 3.2.2 The general correlation case: A verification argument ‚Ä£ 3.2 Optimal strategy for the exponential utility maximization problem ‚Ä£ 3 Merton‚Äôs portfolio problem: Utility maximisation ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models"))) and the weights aj,k+1ia^{i}\_{j,k+1}, bj,k+1ib^{i}\_{j,k+1} are defined as

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | aj,k+1i=őĒőĪiőď‚Äč(őĪi+2)‚Äč{kőĪi+1‚ąí(k‚ąíőĪi)‚Äč(k+1)őĪi,if¬†‚Äčj=0,(k‚ąíj+2)őĪi+1+(k‚ąíj)őĪi+1‚ąí2‚Äč(k‚ąíj+1)őĪi+1,1‚Č§j‚Č§k,1,j=k+1,a^{i}\_{j,k+1}=\frac{\Delta^{\alpha\_{i}}}{\Gamma(\alpha\_{i}+2)}\begin{cases}k^{\alpha\_{i}+1}-(k-\alpha\_{i})(k+1)^{\alpha\_{i}},&\text{if }j=0,\\ (k-j+2)^{\alpha\_{i}+1}+(k-j)^{\alpha\_{i}+1}-2(k-j+1)^{\alpha\_{i}+1},&1\leq j\leq k,\\ 1,&j=k+1,\end{cases} |  |

and

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | bj,k+1i=őĒőĪiőď‚Äč(őĪi+1)‚Äč((k+1‚ąíj)őĪi‚ąí(k‚ąíj)őĪi),0‚Č§j‚Č§k.b^{i}\_{j,k+1}=\frac{\Delta^{\alpha\_{i}}}{\Gamma(\alpha\_{i}+1)}\left((k+1-j)^{\alpha\_{i}}-(k-j)^{\alpha\_{i}}\right),\qquad 0\leq j\leq k. |  |

Here, TT denotes the terminal time or time horizon, nn the number of time steps, and őĒ:=TN\Delta:=\frac{T}{N} the time increment.

Theoretical guarantees for the convergence of this numerical algorithm (the 2-dimensional fractional Adams‚ÄďBashforth‚ÄďMoulton method) are established in Li and Tao ([2009](#bib.bib26)).

## 5 Proofs of the main results

‚ä≥\rhd Preliminaries. As a first preliminary, we state the following Lemma which is an extension to the inhomogeneous setting ([2.2](#S2.E2 "In 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) of the result from (Aichinger and Desmettre, [2021](#bib.bib3), Lemma B.3), which is an enhancement of (Abi Jaber et al., [2021](#bib.bib2), Appendix C). The proof relies on similar arguments and is therefore left to the reader.

###### Lemma 5.1 (Martingale property of stochastic exponentials).

Let WW, W‚ä§W^{\top} be two independent dd-dimensional Wiener processes and VV a weak solution to the inhomogeneous Volterra Square root Equation ([2.2](#S2.E2 "In 2 Preliminaries: Multivariate fake stationary affine Volterra models ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")). Let g1g\_{1} and g2g\_{2} two deterministic processes with values in ‚ĄĚd\mathbb{R}^{d} such that g1,i,g2,i‚ąąL‚ąě‚Äč(‚ĄĚ+,‚ĄĚ)g\_{1,i},g\_{2,i}\in L^{\infty}(\mathbb{R}^{+},\mathbb{R}) for 1‚Č§i‚Č§d1\leq i\leq d. Then the local martingale

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | Zt:=‚Ąį‚Äč(‚ąę0t‚ąĎi=1dg1,i‚Äč(s)‚ÄčVsi‚Äčd‚ÄčWsi+‚ąę0t‚ąĎi=1dg2,i‚Äč(s)‚ÄčVsi‚Äčd‚ÄčWs‚ä§,i)Z\_{t}:=\mathcal{E}(\int\_{0}^{t}\sum\limits\_{i=1}^{d}g\_{1,i}(s)\sqrt{V\_{s}^{i}}dW^{i}\_{s}+\int\_{0}^{t}\sum\limits\_{i=1}^{d}g\_{2,i}(s)\sqrt{V\_{s}^{i}}dW^{\top,i}\_{s}) |  |

is a true martingale.

###### Lemma 5.2 (Martingale property).

Let gg be a deterministic process with values in ‚ĄĚ\mathbb{R} and bounded such that g‚ąąL‚ąě‚Äč([0,T],‚ĄĚ)g\in L^{\infty}([0,T],\mathbb{R}).
Let us denote

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | Zt:=‚Ąį‚Äč(‚ąę0tg‚Äč(s)‚ÄčőĪs‚ä§‚ÄčūĚĎĎBs)=exp‚Ā°(‚ąę0tg‚Äč(s)‚ÄčőĪs‚ä§‚ÄčūĚĎĎBs‚ąí12‚Äč‚ąę0tg2‚Äč(s)‚Äč|őĪs|2‚ÄčūĚĎĎs),t‚ąą[0,T].{Z}\_{t}:=\mathcal{E}(\int\_{0}^{t}g(s)\alpha\_{s}^{\top}\,dB\_{s})=\exp\Big(\int\_{0}^{t}g(s)\alpha\_{s}^{\top}\,dB\_{s}-\frac{1}{2}\int\_{0}^{t}g^{2}(s)\left|\alpha\_{s}\right|^{2}ds\Big),\quad t\in[0,T]. |  | (5.82) |

where (őĪt)t‚ąą[0,T](\alpha\_{t})\_{t\in[0,T]} is a ‚ĄĚd‚ąí\mathbb{R}^{d}- valued process belonging to LūĚĒĹ2,l‚Äčo‚Äčc‚Äč([0,T],‚ĄĚd){L^{2,loc}\_{\mathbb{F}}([0,T],\mathbb{R}^{d})}. Then (Zt)t‚ąą[0,T](Z\_{t})\_{t\in[0,T]} is a martingale.

*Proof:* This is a direct consequence of the fact that g‚ąąL‚ąě‚Äč([0,T],‚ĄĚ)g\in L^{\infty}([0,T],\mathbb{R}) and őĪ‚ąąLūĚĒĹ2,l‚Äčo‚Äčc‚Äč([0,T],‚ĄĚd)\alpha\in{L^{2,loc}\_{\mathbb{F}}([0,T],\mathbb{R}^{d})} together with Novikov‚Äôs condition.‚ąé

We recall here the definition of one dimensional functional resolvent of the first kind of an integral kernel KK in the
terminology of (B. Gripenberg and Saavalainen, [1990](#bib.bib4), Def. 5.5.1) (which can also be found e.g. in Abi Jaber et al. ([2019](#bib.bib1))). Given K‚ąąLl‚Äčo‚Äčc1‚Äč(‚ĄĚ+)K\in{L}^{1}\_{loc}(\mathbb{R}\_{+}), a function rr belonging to Ll‚Äčo‚Äčc1‚Äč(‚ĄĚ+){L}^{1}\_{loc}(\mathbb{R}\_{+}) ( measure L on ‚ĄĚ+\mathbb{R}\_{+}) is called functional resolvent of the first kind of KK if

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | (K‚čÜr)‚Äč(t)=(r‚čÜK)‚Äč(t)=1,(K\star r)(t)=(r\star K)(t)=1, |  | (5.83) |

for all t‚ąą‚ĄĚ+t\in\mathbb{R}\_{+}.
Note that the same notion
can be defined for higher dimensions and in matrix form as follows: Let K‚ąąLloc1‚Äč(‚ĄĚ+,‚ĄĚd√ód)K\in L^{1}\_{\mathrm{loc}}(\mathbb{R}\_{+},\mathbb{R}^{d\times d}) and let RR be an ‚ĄĚd√ód\mathbb{R}^{d\times d}-valued measure on ‚ĄĚ+\mathbb{R}\_{+}.
Then RR is called the resolvent of the first kind of KK if

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  | K‚ąóR=R‚ąóK‚Č°I,K\*R=R\*K\equiv I, |  | (5.84) |

where II denotes the dd-dimensional identity matrix.

###### Lemma 5.3.

Let f,g:‚ĄĚ+‚Üí‚ĄĚf,g:\mathbb{R}\_{+}\to\mathbb{R} be two locally bounded Borel function, let K‚ąąLl‚Äčo‚Äčc1‚Äč(L‚Äče‚Äčb‚ĄĚ+)K\!\in L^{1}\_{loc}(Leb\_{\mathbb{R}\_{+}}) and let r‚ąąLl‚Äčo‚Äčc1‚Äč(L‚Äče‚Äčb‚ĄĚ+)r\!\in L^{1}\_{loc}(Leb\_{\mathbb{R}\_{+}}) be its functional resolvent of the first kind. Then,

1. (a)(a)

   The Volterra Equation of the first kind
   ‚ąÄt‚Č•0,f‚Äč(t)=‚ąę0tK‚Äč(t‚ąís)‚Äčx‚Äč(s)‚ÄčūĚĎĎs\forall\,t\geq 0,\quad f(t)=\int\_{0}^{t}K(t-s)x(s)ds
   (also reading f=K‚ąóxf=K\*x) has a solution given by:

   |  |  |  |  |
   | --- | --- | --- | --- |
   |  | ‚ąÄt‚Č•0,x‚Äč(t)=(‚ąę0tf‚Äč(t‚ąís)‚Äčr‚Äč(d‚Äčs))‚Ä≤that is,x‚Äč(t)=(f‚čÜr)‚Ä≤‚Äč(t).\forall\,t\geq 0,\quad x(t)=\Big(\int\_{0}^{t}f(t-s)r(ds)\Big)^{\prime}\;\quad\text{that is,}\quad x(t)=(f\star r)^{\prime}(t). |  | (5.85) |

   This solution is uniquely defined on ‚ĄĚ+\mathbb{R}\_{+} up to d‚Äčtdt-a.e.a.e. equality.
2. (b)(b)

   The resolvent kernel rr satisfies the following convolution identity:

   |  |  |  |  |
   | --- | --- | --- | --- |
   |  | ‚ąÄt‚Č•0,‚ąę0t(f‚čÜr)‚Ä≤‚Äč(t‚ąís)‚Äč(K‚čÜg)‚Äč(s)‚ÄčūĚĎĎs=‚ąę0tf‚Äč(t‚ąís)‚Äčg‚Äč(s)‚ÄčūĚĎĎs=(f‚čÜg)‚Äč(t)\forall\,t\geq 0,\quad\int\_{0}^{t}(f\star r)^{\prime}(t-s)(K\star g)(s)ds=\int\_{0}^{t}f(t-s)g(s)ds=(f\star g)(t) |  | (5.86) |

We provide a proof of this classical result for the reader‚Äôs convenience.

Proof:
The first claim in ([5.85](#S5.E85 "In item (a) ‚Ä£ Lemma 5.3. ‚Ä£ 5 Proofs of the main results ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models")) follows by the associativity of
the convolution and applying the fundamental theorem of calculus. For the second claim, we could use
calculus of convolutions and resolvents. However, we rather used Laplace transform and deduce that:

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  | L((f‚čÜr)‚Ä≤‚čÜ(K‚čÜg))‚Äč(t)=t‚ÄčLf‚čÜr‚Äč(t)‚ÄčLK‚čÜg‚Äč(t)=t‚ÄčLf‚Äč(t)‚ÄčLr‚Äč(t)‚ÄčLK‚Äč(t)‚ÄčLg‚Äč(t)=Lf‚Äč(t)‚ÄčLg‚Äč(t)=Lf‚ąóg‚Äč(t).L\_{\big((f\star r)^{\prime}\star(K\star g)\big)}(t)=tL\_{f\star r}(t)L\_{K\star g}(t)=tL\_{f}(t)L\_{r}(t)L\_{K}(t)L\_{g}(t)=L\_{f}(t)L\_{g}(t)=L\_{f\*g}(t). |  |

where the penultimalte equality come from applying laplace transform to equation [5.83](#S5.E83 "In 5 Proofs of the main results ‚Ä£ On Utility Maximization under Multivariate Fake Stationary Affine Volterra Models"). We next conclude by the injectivity of Laplace transform. ‚Ė°\Box
